Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	When the color of blood is calmed and the wound has closed, if you return to your work, until the stone is forced out.
de hernie carnouse	De hernie carnouse.
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing else but an assembly of moisture or white sap, which is as soft as the kernels of corn, that contains the egg; and it is called "sap" and never properly exists in the yolk of the egg, if we take care that this is not another work; and this is the skin of the kernel between the white sap that we have mentioned.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this radish is weak, and comes from the kernels, and is spread out in that matter.</start_of_turn>
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	Under no circumstances should percussion be applied to the bones, for this moisture has many colors: or it is pale yellow, or without red, or black, or pale blue, and this is more; and these are the signs of gangrene in this assembly, for if it is white or soft as we have said, if the abscess is round like an egg, and it does not open the bones, because there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the flesh itself, if the abscess bursts with a portion of the yolk, it is thought to be another disease; and if the moisture is between the skin of the groin and the white fat, if he feels well; then when you see the color of the moisture, if you suspect that it has all been discharged, since its form is as before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to that which comes after the introducer, judge that which is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we draw the carbuncles with fire, if we think the patient is cured according to some poor people and the filling of his flesh; then we bind him on his back, on something high, and put a basin under him; then we sit on his left side, and command the minister to sit on his right side, and stretch out his arm to the second rib below the groin; then we take the sponge soaked in vinegar, and cut the skin of the groin among his thighs as far as the white fat; and we tear the skin straight down to the white fat, and we burn it secretly as before; then we pierce the white fat with a needle at a large hole, and drain all the liquid, and then put on our sponges, and stretch out the white fat upwards; and do not touch the groin bone, but only the white fat; cut off all or in pieces immediately the cost of him secretly, if you do not cut it well he will return the liquid; and if the yolk spurts from your wound, keep it in its place until you have completed the work of the white fat; then assemble the two bones of the groin at a joint, and cure him as the others.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	If you find the yellow bile corrupted by another disease, then you must tie up the veins that are suspended, doubting the discharge of blood; then cut off the limb at all the suspension, drain the bile, and cure as we have said.</start_of_turn
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the wound is gathered in two parts together, its edges that are two branches; if you cut the other part as you did the first equally, then wipe the blood away and put in the wound a layer of soft linen soaked in rose oil; and put upon it another layer of linen soaked in wine and oil, and put upon the two edges two nails, and put under it doubled cloths, and bind it up according to this form.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths and use coarse wool yarn in this manner and sew them together at the waist of the braies; and one of the nails grasps on the foundation up to the back, and the other at the painful part; and the other two nails on the two angles, and when they are all assembled, the restriction is in the loop of the brazier; and never is medicine applied for this burn except for the size of a needle; and take only one needle with a fine point, and cut the leather of the nails, and when it is done as we have said, if the white substance which contains the blood is discovered; if you take the burn in this manner, and pierce that membrane as we have commanded, and burn with this fine needle.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And so it must be done in every way possible, until you have achieved your goal; and keep that the fire does not touch the egg; and see that this work is more soothing; and keep guard of the discharge of blood, more than the works of size; and if anything opposes you, or incisions or discharges of blood or anything else that contradicts, cure that which contradicts you, as it is said above.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is pale and does not wish to wait for this work because of its horror, if you deem it necessary, as I have said, and when you are certain by the signs that we have mentioned that the aquous solution is sufficient, if you make the patient sit on a low chair; then pierce the abscess at the lower part with a large needle, and make the perforation through to the bone; and let the wound be large enough that all the pus comes out; then put cotton on the wound and bind it, and leave to drain the remaining fluid, and cure until the wound is healed; and if the cloth does not stop the bleeding from the wound, it is necessary to drink a penny or the instrument with which the hydropic liquid is treated, as it is formed before; and enlarge the wound and see that the bleeding returns, and reassemble after six months or when it is convenient, and when it is reassembled as before, the patient will recover his health.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the buttocks
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Hair that is in the root of this twig has doubt and fear in many places, for I believe that it is worth leaving alone; and I shall tell you the work and the signs of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Therefore, abscesses often come about by swelling or foreign bodies, and it is mostly by chance.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is known by superfluous swelling and pain, which is spread as with wounds; and it is the color of an abscess according to the color of the flesh; and it causes no pain, and is an abscess of grief; and by chance it is a wound that is painful, bloody and purulent, and of dark color, and never comes from a vein, or from an inflamed vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is not from a vein, if it is known by the arrangement of the abscess that it is painful, when you touch it; and I do not know anything other than that you must not touch it
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who makes an embolism of a vein is known by his disposition to the expression of pain in the two thighs; and he can make as well of this semblance as of the others; and it is only that you must take caution like the owners of coions, then the egg is up, and the thread is out of the white substance, and release the suspender from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already clotted with these veins, then you must only draw out the egg, and take hold; and if it is in the white or in what is in the vessels, you must draw out all that is in there, and take hold roundly
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if it is at the jaw or in the bones behind, you must remove all that is tense, and pull out the tooth, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	When your work is done, if you apply a bandage of fine wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then cure it with other remedies until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the buttocks
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess covered with a covering resembling a barrel, with the softening of the bones, and the patient groans loudly when he walks; and the cure for this disease is just as painful as this one that I have mentioned before, and all that we say about it is the work of an old man, according to what he does.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	You must make the patient sit on the edge of the seat, and then suspend the clothes from the waist down to the groin, and grasp them firmly, and extend them forward; then cut through the scrotum with a wide incision to uncover the testicles, and then draw out the testicles, as we have said in the extraction of arteries from the temples; then insert an awl or double thread and tie it to the first testicle or to the root where the thread has come, and tie the other end to the other testicle; then cut around them squarely, according to the length of the cords, and remove the corrupted humors; then cure the wound as usual or apply a bandage, so that no vessel is torn except for those which have already bled; for by this means there will be no harm, and if all the vessels are bled, you must draw out the testicles from all the vessels; so that they do not lose their nourishment from the incision of the vessels, and dry and do not suffer.
de la routure dou syfac	From the root of the wound.
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The coming of this root is by section that comes or by swelling above the belly in the part of the spleen, for the intestines descend from that route to one of the kidneys; and this route is either by swelling or by extension of the liver, and these two methods are of two causes: by percussion, or by jumping, or by pressure, or by the elevation of grief fear, and by similar things; and the sign when it is by swelling of the spleen is that there is swelling and swelling in length, and does not come immediately; and the swelling is equal throughout, for the spleen presses the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign is when the jaw is fractured, that it causes sudden pain in the cheek, and the abscesses are various in appearance, such as skin swelling, and it is because of the discharge of the intestine and the tension of the jaw.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never are the bones displaced with the intestine, and is retained when pressure is put on it, and causes great pain to the patient, even when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these fiery cures with fear, for it is known that they are dangerous.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	If you command or the patient recommends that the intestine be held in his hand within the wound, if it can be returned; then either saw on his collar between your hands, and keep the thighs; then extend the thumb upwards, and cut all the skin of the kidneys along; then enter from the belly of the size of an olive according to what you must master to open the wound, and be such that the intestines do not escape; then pull out the spleen that is outside the skin of the kidneys, until the white spleen is uncovered from all sides; then bring your index finger into that which teaches the kidney, in that which is between the white spleen which is outside the skin of the egg, and between the second spleen, and depart that which is behind the egg, and between the second spleen; and then move the thumb to the right hand inside the kidney, and bring the white spleen to the top of your left hand, and keep the egg to the whole of the spleen towards the size; and command the minister to extend the egg upwards, and unhook that which is behind the ligament; and inquire at your shoulders if there is any intestine or white spleen hardened, and if you find nothing, if it goes to the belly outside; then take a needle or there is a thick thread made of X threads, and pass it in the back part of the spleen, which is after the skin of the kidneys; after the size, then cut the threads that appear from the threads, until there are three threads; and assemble them one on top of the other in the form of a cross, and bind the spleen, of which we have said that it is outside the skin of the kidneys, with a strong thread of two parts; and cover the threads with the threads, and bind them in two parts, so that no vessel that supports them can enter into the wound, except in the case of an embolism that does not arise; and put the thread back in place according to the first thread along two shoulders; and after these two threads leave the spleen that is outside the kidney the greatest of a thumb; and after all the rest according to the roundness that the egg carries; then cut in the part that is outside the skin of the kidneys, as much as it does without repair, and bow; as we have said before; then mix wool soaked in oil, and put them in the wound, and mix the thread that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never cauterize the flesh except as we have said, after the incision, in case of doubt of bloodletting.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For in this matter there are often evacuations of blood, and the limb remains hanging there as long as it aches; and if it lingers too long, even if it arises from a hot bath, put on that which we have said, until it aches; then treat the wound with another treatment, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	De hernie carnouse.
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this chapter I have never seen anyone cure by the iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the old people say that it is made just like the twig which binds the nut, in part as you tie up the blood vessels, after the size above lightly downwards; then take hold of me, and treat the abscess of that which causes it, until the blood vessels cease to bleed; and treat as we have said, until it is perfectly healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Never comes a rupture of the spleen, as we have said, and open the belly; and do not touch any intestines as they are connected, and if you do touch them, that is enough, and repair at once; and whatever remains if it lingers too long in this place, if you believe the wound or the spleen, until the intestines are detached; and this comes from the extension of the spleen which is in the abdomen, as we have said, because it is swollen, then is softened and relaxed and open; and treat as we have said, and never treat with iron in this manner: and let the patient lie still on his back between your hands, and then grasp the belly of the rupture and stretch it out to a width of three fingers; and then remove the spleen which is outside the skin that covers it, then take hold of the needle and remove the part of the spleen that appears; and press at the bottom of the belly, and cut the two ends of the spleen that appear on the top of the needle, and cut one and the other; and then remove the head of the needle, and do not touch the spleen or extend the belly or do anything else, as I have told you in the treatment of the root of the intestines; and then treat with the treatment for wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cauterize the hair, if the pus boils and heals the wound, as long as it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The swelling is constrained, and shows no sign on the surface, and the cautery is mute in this limb, and the more proximate to health.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the joints.
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the joints is softened in sick persons, because the marrow which is within is softened, and it is seen; and it is necessary, when one sees it cured, to make the patient sit up on his back, and to cut the softened skin over the natural skin; then join the two layers of the skin with sutures, and if you see, close the superfluous softened skin with two or three stitches firmly; then press between the sutures, and cure like the other wounds, until it is healed, and cut the thread.
dou chastrement	Dou chastrement.
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Saiches that are deemed useless in our laws, and for this reason I do not wish to speak of them in this book; and it is not necessary to force anyone to do so. For one, the patient’s eye responds when asked. And the other, we often mix up the cautery of various beasts with our assistants, as with a goat, sheep, cat, and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that cautery is done in two ways: by traction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the traction method, we make the limb lie in hot water, until the bone softens and swells; then we grasp the limb with our hand until it is reset and no longer painful
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	From the armpit: command that you hold the arm firmly, and press the skin of the armpits to your left hand, then bind the dressing, and support each limb with a support, when you have well secured them; and leave no trace of sweat or visible sweat which is on the blood vessels; and this method of cautery is milder than that which is made by attraction, because by attraction remains by chance no hair, for which the best desire is luxury; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	des hermofrodites.
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism is according to two manners as in the home: one if between the two testicles there appears as much as the nature of a woman, or if there are hairs, and sometimes in court it urinates.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, and has on the navel as much as a boy and two testicles
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for the bite of an animal is that you cauterize the hairs all around; and you treat it like other wounds. In the second method, of those whose urine spurts through the pores of the skin, if there is no remedy.
de la tentigene	Hermaphrodism is in two ways as in women: one if between the two testes opens as with the figure of the nature of a woman, or if there is hair, and sometimes in the urine is retained. And the other way if it is in women, and has on the navel as a beard and two testes. And the cure of the womb and fame if it is that you crush the testicles completely, and the cure is like other wounds; in the second way, of those homes whose urine leaps through the skin of the testes, if there is no cure.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tenacity is a bite that is too violent for the natural part, as women often have as much pain as a hand; and this is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you hold the excess of the bite of your hand or genitals firmly; and touch it lightly; and do not go too deep, for blood does not come from there; then treat with other medicines until it is healed; and for another bite that comes from the mouth of the marrow, and the spleen, and by chance spurts out, and is like a wound, and for this reason it is called the old "coward's disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you think you have cured it, as we have said before, continue the treatment until it is healed.
de erratique	De erratique.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	If it is uncertain whether the woman is well or poorly conceived, or if the rupture is small; or if it is by birth or by disease that comes from it; or if it is by a clot of blood or a thick or thin blood-vessel, and is made in the marrow, or the ribs, or the spleen, or any other place; then it must be suspected, and the conception must be known by observing the woman's behavior.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If swelling appears nearby, either on the side or on the other, it is nearby
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a thick blood-vessel, and it is nearby as two fingers, if you are in a hurry, and it has burst: put your two index fingers together, and the woman lying on her back, spreading out her legs; then the two fingers push, as long as the thick blood-vessel is round, and is over the swelling; then take a cloth, soak it in oil, and put it on the wound, and keep the woman still at rest, until it has healed.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the scapula is hard and thick, it is good that you grasp it with a sponge resembling a laurel leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is stamped with charcoal, if you suspend it on the incision and grasp it; and have the medicines that are staying still, such as acaice, dragon's blood, incense, and lots of eggs; then mix in a plaster of lead wide, so that the wound does not stick; and let it be long, and mix in a lint of hemp. Then do other cures until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when charcoal comes to the marrow, if you cover it as this method suggests, this is not for abscesses.</start_of_turn
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the abscess in the marrow, do not touch fire.</start_of_turn
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Emorroydes are open veins which do not usually heal without treatment; and when old, they become thick and tough. We have already mentioned the signs and symptoms of such wounds; here I will tell you those which are most frequent and which usually lead to recovery.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that when emorroids and the tough parts [blood clots] are buried in the marrow and are not felt, they must be treated with iron to achieve a cure
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those which are in the mouth of the marrow can be felt, and these can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is necessary therefore that you put the woman in a cold house, then hold the elbow firmly, grasp the joint at its roots, and sprinkle over it restraining medicines such as chamomile and dragon’s blood and incense, and similar things; then bind the limb when it shows signs of healing, then immerse it in cold water; and if blood comes, let it flow into a decoction of sumac and pomegranate peel, and meadowsweet and other things, and then give her barley flour, and mix it with honey and rue, and make a poultice of it and apply it to her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it [the hair] sticks, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If this does not happen, if it makes air bubbles at the back and has worms [meaning boils] that will cause pain; then take lint, and moisten it with the juice of plantain or with the juice of marigold with old wine, and make air to the wound.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the abscess is cured, if you see blood dripping from the wound as long as it is healthy; and the one called "albather" is red, and is similar to a blackhead, if you cover it as I have said previously; then cure until it is healthy again
des apostemes de la marris	Emoroids are openings of veins which without restraint are usually harmless; and when they are old they become tough. And we have already said in the division the signs and symptoms, and I shall now tell you those which are most useful for the cure. I say that emorroids and the tough ones, when they are pressed into the marrow, are not felt, except by the physician. For those which are at the entrance of the marrow, we can feel them, and these we can cure. It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then stretch the heel as much as possible, and press on its root, then sprinkle on restraining medicines such as acacia and dragon’s blood and incense, and similar things; then withdraw the piece an hour later, and put it in cold water; and if there is still pain, if she has taken a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and barley and similar things, and then swallow barley flour, and mix with honey and fennel, and make one application on her back. And if it has stopped bleeding, that is good. If this is not the case, make her lie down with a bandage on her back and apply pressure with a finger; then take a cloth and wet it with the juice of plantain or with the juice of elderberry with wine vinegar, and make her lie down. And when the abscess has subsided, if it is yellow, it is like a rough chief, if it is red, it is like a scab which has been left too long; and in both cases it must be covered as I have said the tough one. And then it must be cured as long as it is sane. And when the abscess has subsided, if it is yellow, it is like a rough chief, if it is red, it is like a scab which has been left too long; and in both cases it must be covered as I have said the tough one.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many ways of abscesses come about in the body, such as carbuncles and pyretic abscesses and herpes and hemorrhoids and fistulas and varicose veins and burned abscesses, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the previous section
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is proper that I should say that I depart from this treatment when the burn comes into the marrow, which is not a burn but which collects pus; and if you know the work of iron, look if the burn is still red at the outset of its coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red, you shall see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Do not be in a hurry, but make me wait until the pain is eased; then make the patient sit on a chair, and put two small cushions or he will recline, and support his back and unite his limbs so that his thighs are spread apart, and put his arms across his knees, and bind them firmly with a bandage; then gently push the bail towards the breastbone, and bring the instrument from which we remove the pus from the marrow, so that this will take its form; and know that when you bring this instrument in, make sure you first ascertain the depth of the marrow, so that what enters with the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is too large, cover the depth of the marrow with a cloth so that the instrument does not hurt it; and make sure that you put the horn of the instrument on the underside, and hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens, and we put a finger to the root, if it covers the head and the armpit, and when the wound is emptied, if you wish, put in the wound some soft wool soaked in rose oil or dry green oil; put the dressing firmly over the wound and over the dressing put on a layer of linen wool soaked in warm or cold water; then cure it after two days of dressing has elapsed from that time, until it is healed; and never remove the dressing and wound with a clip of water and honey, and then with water or licorice root and alum.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound has healed in the wound, if you wish, take care not to burn it, but cure it as we have said before in the division.
de l’enfantement	Many are the causes of inflammation in the marrow, as in chancre and perforated abscess, herpes, swelling, fistula, hemorrhoids, and charred bone, and many other diseases which I mentioned in the division. It is therefore necessary that I speak in this treatment of charred bone that comes in the marrow, which is not an abscess that collects pus only; and if you know the work of iron, look if the abscess is still in its beginning, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red, tell me when you saw it. Do not therefore pierce it immediately, but make me measure the pain until it is appeased; then make the patient sit on a chair, and give him three small stools or make him recline, and support his back and join his limbs as far as the limb is deformed; let his thighs be spread out, and put his arms across his knees, and bind them securely with a strong bandage; then hold the bail towards the lower costal margin, and bring the instrument from which we take the mouth of the marrow, so that this comes after; and know that when you bring this instrument, that you must first feel the depth of the marrow to ensure that what enters does not go deeper than it should and does not harm the patient; and if the instrument is too large, know that you must cover the depth of the marrow with a drape so that the instrument does not touch it; and know that you must put the trumpet of the instrument at its base and hold the instrument. And when the abscess bursts, and we have the hand in, if you know the cover must be applied to the chief and the surrounding area; and when the pus is evacuated, know that you must put in the wound a few soft sponges soaked in rose oil or in dry green oil; put the sponge firmly against the depth of the wound, and put over it and on the wound a clean gauze pad soaked in water or mallow, which must be cooked; then cure after three days following this. And if the wound is closed in the marrow, know that you must be careful not to burn with iron, but cure it as we have said in the division.
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The master first of all must know the figure of natural infancy, and the signs are when you see the woman pressing down on the belly, and desire to smell the breast; then the child hastens to rise; then withdraw the breast that the infant's feeding is according to the natural figure, and comes out from his head, and supports him with his hand; and when you see these signs, if you press slightly on his belly, so that the child comes out headfirst; for when he descends from his head, if he is supported with his hand, and is made whole by his superfluousness.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it never comes except from the feet, or from the arm or hand, or from the belly, or from the side, and is converted by chance from his collar, and by other vicious figures; if the master is at the dance that he is wise and discreet in these matters, and avoids error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how we must help him.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	When the fetus comes down naturally through the head and the woman gives birth fiercely, and her strength is weak, if you make her sit on a chair, or the women hold her; and arise her nature from oil or rue or rue oil, and then continue the play between her thighs the small cushion which is her shape:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And split the secondine, and bind to its nail as long as the moisture that is in its core is fierce; and press the woman’s belly until the fetus descends, and if it does not descend, if you must, clench the woman with muscle of fenugrec with oil of assa; then let her take and expel a condition, and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour: if it is now delivered.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if two hands come out violently, if you must, gently hold them down; and if they will not enter, put the woman on a seat, and keep her feet high; then withdraw the seat from the earth, and hold her, that she does not cry out; and if the hands still will not enter, and the fetus is dead, if you grasp the hands at the shoulder which is in front, and pull out the child, and restore equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	From the issue of the child on his feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes onto his feet, if you can push up; and then twist to and fro, until they are even; then take hold of the feet and stretch to and fro.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If he jumps up to his hips, if the master commands him to take hold, and makes him cough up the phlegm; if he jumps too high, God help him
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if he does not jump up as we have said, if the lord commands and commands, as long as it is in accordance with the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For thus is it rightly done.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if he does not jump so high as we have seen, say that you take muscle from the shoulder, oil of alum, gum mastic, and broth, and grind them all together in a mortar; and put on the nature of the woman inside and take away this swelling, then make her sit in hot water until the ribs are soft; and when she is softened from the water, give her a collar of myrrh, and put on her clothes, and leave her for an hour; then make her sit on her seat, then make her cough and strain her mouth and nose, and take hold of her belly slightly, for the child jumps now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	Then he sits on the edge of the bed, and makes him cough and strain his mouth and his nose, and grasps his belly lightly, for the fetus now leaps from his genitals
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, if he puts his hands on his face and head; then either he is struck on the neck, and the piece of the jaw is hanging down, or he is without support; and he bends his hands on his face and head, and then he grasps his hands under his belly, and he forces the cushions outwards until they appear in the throat; and if the child does not jump, if he grasps his piece and moves it, then he moves his belly upwards, and he lets go of his hands; and the child will be saved and saved; and command the woman to take care of him as long as the child remains.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	because the child’s hand has just gone limp.
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I can teach you to restore the limb: if it cannot be restored, if you make the woman rise up and call for help; if she cannot call for help, if you make her lie down and put her legs out; then mix the medicine that I have told you about; and if she does not improve, if you make her sit on the chair, then study to restore the limb; and when the limb is restored according to its natural shape, make her spit, and command her to take care of him as long as the child remains strong
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	From the issue of the limb from its socket, and has expanded her hands, and her face turned towards her mother’s back.</start_of_turn>
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I command that you grasp his hand firmly, then twist it a little to and fro, and move it lightly; and when it is even, put upon the oily substance of alum and oil, as we have said before, and then command that it move a little to and fro; and when you have done this, seat him upon a chair and command him to grasp; and he will vomit.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in this way throughout the second period of time.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When he comes with force in this manner throughout the secondine, if you seize the secondine at his nail, while the moisture is evacuated; and if it swells up on his face and neck, if you seize it of the abscess, that it be not retained, and the child will die; then take the child out, as you have put it, and command the woman not to move again: thus it will be light.</start_of_turn>
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of the twins.
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Hairs that grow together often do not grow at the same time; two or three do not grow simultaneously. This is not an unusual occurrence, and it often happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	What is strange is that they live without a name; I know well that they are multiplied, and they are driven out by the syfac which is linked to the gut; and never has anything escaped as naturally as all of them, as we have said.

If they escape roughly, if the treatment is as we have said, and if the spirit is tame, and make haste and lightly what she makes; and do as much as you can for your health.</start_of_turn>
de plusors enfans	to drain what is causing it.</start_of_turn>

de l’enfant mort	of a dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you cure a woman of a dead child or an empty womb, if there is no urgency and you are constrained by the workload of your hands; if you suspect that the woman is of sound health, and has no accident or fear of death; if you suspect that the woman is in labor, and her shoulders are clinched, her arms raised and her legs lifted; then touch her navel with two fingers, or bind her to the bed if she is not being treated in the delivery of the child; then smear her mouth with a mixture of mustard, alum, and flaxseed and linseed seeds; then anoint her hands with these oils and these powders; then place them in the womb lightly; then command her to bear down or let her bear down naturally as she is able; and you must hold the medicine in her right hand, and put the thumb between her two fingers of her left hand, and hold her firmly with her entire hand, and insert the medicine into none of the places we have mentioned, until it comes out naturally; puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then the hook finds another bone, or the third if you are in charge, if so the extraction must be even; and then extend them evenly by moving from side to side, for movement itself is sufficient, and the teeth of the hook may be held by hand.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers. And if one hand comes in front of the other, and it cannot be pulled back due to tension, you must cover above the drape, until it is whole; then pull the thumb at the joint of the wrist or the elbow, and you must do the same with the other hand, and there will be two thumbs.

And if the head of the shoulder is large and swollen at the outlet, or if there is an assembled chief's head, if you must join the spinous process between your two thumbs, and grasp the chief and pull out the swelling; or you can roll it with the instrument called "almidach," with which the swelling comes with the abscess or chapter that follows this; and so make the swelling swell naturally; and then treat the bones as tenacious, and when the head of the shoulder leaps up and strains at the forcele, if it is fractured, until the moisture that is or has come out leaps out; and if it cannot be extruded, if the bone breaks in pieces at the muscle that you must break; and if it is inflamed in the belly or along the ribs, if you must break as many ribs as the moisture corrects.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	If it is swollen on the side, if the attraction is strong, and the approach to the root of the marrow is easier.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is swollen in the belly or the arm, it is best to remove the swelling with a drape wrapped around the hand; and hold the belly or the arm until the moisture that is causing it disappears. And if another limb is affected and the bone is displaced, if the limb is pulled from its socket by the force of the hand, treat it until the socket is closed by the callous that has come; for if it cannot be passed through, it must be brought up and out by force. And if the opening of the socket is narrowed by the callous that has come, if it cannot be passed through, it must be dilated with moist and fatty things; and it must be plastered with soft and moist substances.

dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the marrow back to its place

Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, may be made from ebony or boxwood, according to the shape of the nails; and it has two chisels two awls, as you see, of a palm of a long size, and two of a broad size; and when you see opening the mouth of the instrument, make the woman sit I let, the pieces between and the legs over, then join the two awls together in the mouth, and hold the head of the instrument between her thighs; then hold your hand over the instrument, as if you had made the nails even, according to the quantity that you see opening the mouth of the instrument, until the bail makes what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all very slippery, and their resemblance is multiplied in their appearance; and when you see them appear, the more haste there is to open them, and the higher your home is for their quantity.

Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second [tooth] is retained in infancy, if you command the patient to retain the milk tooth, and then make her spit it out of her mouth, and hold your hands over her mouth and nose; and if she spits out for this reason, well done.

If this be not so, take I pot and make I hole or cut; and I put herbs therein that can open the mouth of the mare, as camomile, rue, anis, chamomile, cassia and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, let them be boiled or put in water over the fire; then put in a slug or hole in the pot, and the other head in the mouth of the mare, and bind them until the vapor comes out of the mare; then make her vomit, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the secondine has pricked at its base, hold the eyes steady until they grow

If she comes and becomes quiet again.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	If the mouth of the marrow is swollen, we have said the cure is to cauterize and fumigate with herbs; and if it is not from all that we have said, if you do not use anything else, keep that which is at the mouth of the marrow bound to the hip of the woman, then clench it with oil of tetrafarmaçon; if she bites and relaxes, she will come out whole; but nevertheless, when she comes out, if there is a bad odor from the stomach and head, and she vomits, the patient is cured.

It is like seeing a fox, put the head of the sufferer over the fire; and either fumigate with charcoal, or apply a poultice until it is consumed, and start again.</start_of_turn>
de percier lou fondement	Or let the fumigations be over the charcoal, and the smoke until it is consumed, and begin again.
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the firm basis perceptible, for they have been stamped upon by a subtle syfat: if you command her to dance that she pierce that syfat at her will, and do not let her prick with any sharp object, and keep the dressing that she does not touch; then put on coarse cloth soaked in wine and oil, and cure her with oil until she is healed.

de la fistule dou fondement	of fistula from the root.
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from the foundation are nodules, and those that come from below the foundation deviate, or in the space of two parts, if there is a fistula or several; and when that nodule is old, if it persists, and is accompanied by moisture, white or soft pus, and never are these fistulas permanent; they are known by the fact that there is blood, evacuation or wind during evacuation when the patient defecates, and by chance in a leap.</start_of_turn>
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	If there are fistulas that reach the bladder, and half way up the thigh; and they reach the hip joint, and even the coccyx.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus it is known on the fistula persisting at the base, and does not go away: that you must bite your thumb index or base, and insert a fine needle of spider or iron into the fistula when there is no swelling.

And if there is swelling, if you insert a sponge or horsehair, as long as you feel the swelling or pressure on your thumb; and if you do not feel it, and there is no discharge of blood or wind, as we have said: evacuate the swelling that does not burst; if you delay in curing.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	When the fistula persists until the bladder or urinary tract, if in a leap the urine escapes and cannot be stopped by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is perceived up to the armpit, if the vein is still there; if there is no swelling and the pain subsides, if it has been properly positioned, and there is no medicine or support by ointment; and in these persistent fistulas there is no cure except work, and the vanities of the fools who interfere.</start_of_turn
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In that one which is neither new nor old, hope for health by fire, as I have seen; and that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and he holds his legs up to his hips, and has his hips inclined towards his belly; then make an attempt to pull or plunge if there is pain, until you feel or the attempt comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain at the root of the limb, if you think that you have grasped the bone, if you feel that the attempt has been perceived; either uncover or feel between your thumb and index finger the cartilage or bone, then pull out that which is personal; if this does not suffice, it will not be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One can easily heal almost all ailments, but this is not always the case; and the help which one does make, if one severs the fine cautery according to the size of the fistula, as it is said before; and one fills all around the fistula, until it goes beyond the root; and do this twice or thrice, until you feel that these hairs which are similar to a nail of oil must be burned; and then treat with soft compresses until the hair has fallen out, then treat with oil that binds the hair and closes the wound
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is sane, that is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If he is sane, that is well; for if he attempts between and does not pierce until he reaches the root which is or should be, and between his thumb and the attempt a thick covering of hair or sificate, and you will see the fistula at that which is under the covering as blood; if the copes of the commencement of the fistula, and hold steadily before the attempt, and then cauterize afterwards, until it reaches the head of the attempt; and the attempt will be delivered, and will cease. Then praise the hairs that were required that seemed like a hen’s foot, and nothing remains of them.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	If he does not go away from you, and if you are between him and the work, if you cauterize with fire or medicine that is strong.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery brings together two things: namely, the burning of these hairs above-mentioned, and the coagulation of blood and the drying of moisture; then the cure of wounds with soft sponges or broken chaff, until the blood flows freely; and then cauterize the hairs which are burned in the flow of blood; then cure the wound of suppuration with dry sponge and these are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, if it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if an abscess comes up to the root of the bone, and is loosened from the flesh, if the bone or root remains loose, inquire about that.</start_of_turn>
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If thou feel the attempt, and between the second and the third there is the thread or the flesh or bone, or it is near to pierce, if there is no greater force than the way of escape and hope, by the administration of one of the three methods: or thou cauterize it as we have said, or thou bind it until the end, or if thou do thus put thy hand to the test and cure as before; and do not fear too much, that thou cover only that which holds the foundation, and let the evacuation go in the natural way; then cure as before; by chance if it be well, or thou drain that covering and the mucus then when it is bound from the foundation, or by attempt or by other pointed instrument; then tie up that which is necessary in the wound, as thou do; then study to restore the wound, and to stop the fistula in the part following the foundation: if it be a lighter thing to the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And never are fistulas in this manner: when you bite the attempt at the fistula, and it is either cost or extends deeply from the leather below, if you take a bite pierced at the head according to this fashion:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And there is always a thread torn in two, and the attempt is at the whole thread in the fistula until it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	And never are fistulas in this manner: when you bite the attempt at the fistula, and it is either cost or extends deeply from the leather below, if you take a bite pierced at the head according to this fashion: if it is perforated at the root of the foundation, then draw out the thread of that which is perforated, so that you bite your thumb or foundation; and draw out the head of the thread, and reunite the two bones together, and restrain one to the other, and leave it for one or two; and do not restrain it ever again, until the thread has stopped these hairs that are between the two, and that are itching; then cure the wound until it is healed and healthy.
