Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not burst, if you force it to break in all the ways you can, it will not be too much damaged.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not right to make the wound wider by force, and then to cure it as we have said, when it is still sound.</start_of_turn>
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spiky nipple from which the fistula is made is moist and thick with one part, but trenchant; and on the other hand not, for in this case we must not grasp that which we must not grasp. If you see this:
des emorroydes	Des emorroydes.
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racine; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you agree that you must bring the shoulder close to this manner: take I thread of silk, and pierce it with a needle, and then pass the thread through below and make the needle pierce through the other side, and take II threads of silk from the needle, and if they are thick; tighten the thread forming, then knot the thread, and pull out the needle, and make secure all the others, and leave I to correct the excess of blood; then put on the foundation I bandage slightly damped in rose oil or cerate, and put on the foundation, and command the patient to rest; and then leave it until it aches, and when it is sore, if the cure of oil and other cure, until it is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	while the itching has ceased or the foundation has been secured
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	There are often spasms of the bowels, and by constriction of nature, and when the disease is advanced and medicine is of no avail.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you notice at the point of a scab or at your nail the scale below, which does not allow it to moisten; then cure it until it is healed if it is possible; and if it cannot be healed, if you must renew the shaving more strongly than before, until it bleeds, and be scraped away; then cure it until it is healed.
dou fremit	but let him groan.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formice is a small outgrowth that grows forward from the limb, and goes out towards the edge of the wound; and never does the trueve touch it, and it is felt as though dead from fear, and comes over the whole limb, and more than in any other part.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a piece of goose quill, or a piece of strong vinegar, and put that salve on the wound, until the circle turns blue around the wound; then turn your hand over the entire wound until you have embraced it all around the wound, and put it out towards the edge, and scrape the wound from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if thou seest, if thou do this with a needle of spider or of iron as it is said, and be subtle and attentive:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if thou seest, if thou do this with a needle of spider or of iron as it is said, and be subtle and attentive, do not perceive [the movement of the eye], for to keep it still, and to press [the eye] lightly. And if thou seest, if thou cauterize the limb, if it is before or alongside the cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	and if thou seest, if thou do this with a needle of spider or of iron as it is said, and be subtle and attentive, do not perceive [the movement of the eye], for to keep it still, and to press [the eye] lightly. And if thou seest, if thou cauterize the limb, if it is before or alongside the cautery, do this of the form of a cluster.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never make a cluster of silver or gold, or of spider’s blood melted or molten; and never make of these small and great things according to these to which they are subject.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those who suffer from fevers and who are weak and painful are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	Their form is small and great if it is due to a wide belly, or the belly is bound according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if there is a swelling or the belly is tied, if you see, and the shoulder is either pierced or cut; and there are two holes at one side of the breastbone, and one at the other; or if the belly or abdomen has medicine in a bladder of gut or parchment, or is pierced all around with numerous holes, and there is one inch of space between each hole, then put in this hole one strong thread of strong thread twisted in the shape of an X or around the belly, and assemble the belly as if it were a nail; and when the medicine is inside, if there is an instrument in front of a strong thread, then clip it; and this is the shape of a circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold; anoint the head with a cluster of oil or balm of egg, or something like that, then bind it lightly; then grasp the minister with both hands together, until it is fully visible, then draw out the cluster, and leave the patient his legs exposed, and if the medicine sees that it is sufficient, if the patient sleeps all night, that is more effective.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he puts it to the test in a case of wound of the belly, and the physician hastens to leave, if he returns as long as he is well.</start_of_turn>
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if there is swelling of the limb or wound, or abscess, if the cluster is as subtle as for one child; that is the form of a subtle cluster when the skin is strained:
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already mentioned in this chapter the treatment of wounds; or rather the treatment of hands and medicines, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse depending on how they are made, and depending on the parts of the body or the wounds themselves, and how they are made
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things that cause wounds are bites of stone, and the size of spear and nail, or lance or fist or sickle, or similar things; or that are made according to the rules of the body, as for a wound that bites on the neck, or on the head, or the shoulder, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the cure for a wound of the head and I will begin with simple wounds because the memory will come to mind in this chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound occurs or a dislocation, and the bone is not fractured, take care if it is from a wound or from something else, and the skin is entirely ruptured and the wound is large, and you doubt the depth of the wound: if you do the same thing too often, you will make the patient sicker from the head downwards even if there is blood coming from the wound itself; or let the blood flow in the opposite direction of the part affected; and listen to the patient’s complaint of thirst for wine and meat.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he does not recover, if he is nourished only with meat, and does not drink wine, does not eat cheese; and take out the wound, if there is pus coming from it, cover the wound loosely with soft cotton or oiled rose ointment, or in styptic wine; and if there is no deeper wound, put on the wound itself, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by air, dust, or anything else; and if it has been moved, put on some ointment until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a spear and similar, and the limbs do not join together by tension, if you join them with stitches, as I will say, for wounds like those of the belly, with stitches.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed by a bone fragment, and it is painful, and only held by a piece of cartilage; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore flesh in place of skin, and command the patient to eat coarse food, such as testicles and bread, as well as poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	If you find or see a broken piece of bone, if it does not penetrate the bone, if you can move it out whole, and you can drain the swelling, then treat it; and if there is a blood vessel in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped by medicine, if it is an artery, and if you find it dislocated, if it is held by a thread; and if this does not help, if you must, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, if it is a light cure: then put in this powder which adheres as soon as it has moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The method of the powder is as follows: take incense one part; dragon’s blood two parts; live chalk three parts, and grind them together; and use the powder liberally, and strain the wound, until it is well closed and reunited with all its blood; and then bind it firmly, and leave it until it heals, if it does not swell; for we do not dress the medicine until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never do we do this charcoal treatment alone, when we have no incense or blood of a dragon, but only when the wound has not moved.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound has moved, even in this state, if one does not put on this powder; but put upon some unguents digestible, or poultices of ground barley made of water and honey, until it stops bleeding; then treat with other cures until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a fracture occurs with the wound, and it is small, if you grasp the wound with fine tweezers; and I will tell you about fractures later on.</start_of_turn>
de la plaie dou col	of the collarbone.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	The wound comes from the collarbone and it is simple, if there is no difference between it and the fracture of the skull, but if the collarbone or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If the nerve is affected, if there is no other ailment except to leave the cure alone, and do not put anything restraining, because it hinders the nerve and makes it recede; and do not put anything rough on the wound, for the substance of the nerve is cold, and the continuation of the pain is with the marrow, which is the most hollow limb; but if the medicine is soft, like lukewarm water with sweet oil, and honey mixed with rose oil, and vinegar washed in sweet water, and other stones of mine according to this manner, and moist unguents.</start_of_turn>
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, if the bone and sinew are bent, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	If wounds are deep and the flesh is swollen and full of boils, if the wound is pierced or lower in the limb; and if an artery is severed, blood flows profusely; if the bone is fractured, and the marrow and the cauterization mingle, if the wisdom tooth is pierced, or the tonsils, and the tongue is retained, because the meat hangs there; if the shoulder blade is pierced, or the ribs, and the gut is held, because the meat goes there, if the rib above the collarbone is broken, do not touch the throat but restore it to its natural position; then stretch it out again, and leave it alone for a while, then cure the wound with gentle pressure until it is healed; and if there is a piece of bone, if the fragments are numerous and you cannot have them all out, leave as much as possible, and let the wound heal and align naturally.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is fistula, if the wound is treated as I have said in the chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of from a wound of a lance or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it be from a lance or a knife, and the wound is deep, if you behold that the wound has burst open violently as if a wound of death; and if it be not deep, and it is fresh throughout its entirety, do not put anything at the first hour the powder, do not bind it up with the blood lest it worsen; remove it, and comfort the patient; but put in an astringent, and bind it twice; if there be no astringent, put into the wound fine cotton to soak up the moisture, and let the patient rest upon the wound for three days, or four, or more; if there be no spasm, do not move or strain the limb. When you see the bones arranged, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the boils and other cures, as long as they are sane; and if they cannot be cured, and if there is an opening, draw out the pus that there is a fistula; if the cure is as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is an incision of a spear or knife, and it is simple, or worse at the front or back, if the cure of what is before; if it is great, with sutures; and if it is small, with powder, and if it is stuck in the bone, and it has broken pieces, if you want the wound, and the threads will burst if they are taut; and if they are not taut, if you leave the wound open, if it aligns with the extractions; and for other wounds, as for other members, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	indeed
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The belly is greatly and moderately swollen; from a great wound never does the intestine go out, neither does it come out of the intestines; for the intestines are driven inwards by the tumors; and the pain is greater in the large wounds than in the small, because they cause the intestines to go out more; so that the intestines swell up so much that they feel the fruit; when they go out more, the great wound is more painful; for the intestines must be drawn back to their place as before. The intestines are twisted in three ways: the two common costures arise in the belly costure, and the other two costures are common with other wounds; all of them are greater with the belly costure.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestines is protruding, and there is pain, this is to be remedied in one of two ways: either by the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen from the fruit.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, soak the limb in a mild part: moisten a sponge or I put a drape in lukewarm water only, or you shall burn in lukewarm water squealing and spitting and pricking, and raise the intestine as long as the swelling is bony; and do not make this wine restrictive, and be quiet that awe soul for deflating.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see swelling depart, if moisten the intestine with water or raise and burn them slightly, because by this is the entrance to things; and if it cannot enter, if make an opening at the instrument of cutting off the hemorrhoids; and the first cure is quiet that the size, that we must not cut without great necessity, and that is the instrument for cutting: if it tears from within the curve and does not come out, and see to this shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is swollen, and the intestines are protruding, if you stop the bleeding according to its natural form in its own place, you will have done well, for this is worth doing.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And when the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the belly, if you must manage the patient on his back, and raise his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the lower part of the belly, if you put the head and the heel higher than the lower parts, and if the pain of the belly is in one of the two lower parts, if you put the upper part higher than the lower one; then you must understand what I say in great and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	In small wounds, put these things that appear between your hands I apply pity which holds all the wound to its hand, and gather the lips; and this is the common manner of stitching, and that you take a needle or more, according to the quantity of the wound, then leave a space at the head of the wound I must, and I pierce the two holes of the skin with the two holes of the needle, which is from the inside of the skin, as long as you make it pierce through that part, and gather the two heads of the needle together; then I strain a double thread around the needle at two parts, then gather the two holes of the wound together, and then leave a space, and I pierce another needle; then I bind the thread as you did the first needle, and do not cease doing this until all the wound is restrained; and let the needles be neither too thick nor too thin, for the thick needles will clog all the flesh, and the too thin will not be able to enter well; for this reason you must make them neither too thick nor too thin; and do not push the needles too far from the flesh and from the skin, that they clog and open the wound before the suture; and then close the holes of the needles, that they do not bleed the patient at night, and put patches or bandages over the holes of the needles for to hold them, and leave them until the wound is healed; and this method of stitching with needles is more convenient in small wounds, for there is only one needle or two at most for the second suture, and that you gather the two holes of the skin and the two holes of the needle together with a needle or there is one strong thread medium; and when you have pierced these things together, three in total, gather the needle at the part or where you began, in the manner in which you cut the threads. And leave space between each stitch the thickness of a small fist; this stitch will suffice for the home, and I stitched a wound once upon a time for a wound which was navel-born from a knife, and the wound was more than a palm of great, and there were intestines well two palms of great, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I will return the intestines when they have been out for twenty-four hours, and the wound will be closed after fifteen days, and the treatment will be completed, and he will be healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And he saw that he was going to die, and this was a miracle; and I did not treat him with any medicine, for I was in India where there is no doctor, no medicines; and I put on more ointment on the wound twice a day, and I gave him honey until he was healed.</start_of_turn>
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or you will tell me two ways to suture: take the needle and pass it through the back part until you reach the underside; when it has pierced the right knuckle to the right, if the thread slips or breaks or you have passed the needle, and you must pierce again from the underside until you reach the back; and you understand this stitching if you sew like a leatherworker and leave one thread on one side and take it up again on the other, until the stitching is complete.</start_of_turn
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of stitching, which Galiens does with great care, if it is so with anyone else, who assemble the two parts naturally, and apply one of the chief ends to the other chief, in part: pierce a needle or chief of the neighbouring area, and make it pierce only that which is below, and leave the two chief ends; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the lower part until it reaches this far side, with two chief ends; then make it pierce one and the other from the lower part until it reaches this far side, in two other chief ends that are on the other side; and this is the wisest method of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galiens says this by word, and no one testifies to it, we must sew the belly with two needles, or there is yarn in the bobbin; and we must push one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew wounds; and stitches that when the wound is turned it is inside the belly, if the stitching is greater than others on the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judge of the wound is like the judge of other wounds: that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, even if it has moved, if you stop the intestines and the gut; then put on the healing powder and char, and if it has moved, do not put on any ointment that is present, until the wound has healed; then close the wound, and be sure to ligate the vessels and nerves, and the muscle; then cure the wound like the others, until it is healed. And if you have no medicines, just put on, as soon as it begins to ooze blood, cotton wool, and move it twice the number of times that it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	You need no other medicine in many cases except for simple wounds; and if you doubt that the wound will not heal properly, moisten coarse linen with warm oil of poppies or rose oil, and apply it to the wound, and bandage the edges; and if there is pain or putrefaction in the belly, and it happens many times, if you give it clusters of black vinegar, and in the same way if the putrefaction comes up to the intestines; and prick through, and drain that when the large intestine is full, it is easier to heal than the small intestine.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines which are called "jeuns" cannot heal when they are swollen, because of the stretching of the veins, and for the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if there is a burst wound, if you return it back as soon as the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is black and becometh towards or black, if you tie the black part, do not remove the blood, for there are veins and arteries there; then close what is between the layers, and hang the two shoulders down from the part below the wound until the burst has fled, in order to align the extraction when the wound bursts, and the wound will bow
de la routure dou boueil	because of the route of the boil.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is round, and the wound is small, if you can restore it in a quiet place, because I have seen that one bone has been swollen or pierced by a lance; and the wound was at the stomach, and became filled and became a fistula, and in this there was egestion and wind; I treated it as I thought best, and did not cease to subtilize until it was healed, and the wound closed
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I see it soldered, I doubt that the patient has anything wrong in his belly; and there is no point of harm, but many good arrangements, food and drink; and they say that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be ligatured in parts: take tweezers and grasp the edges of the wound, and when the tweezers have passed over the opening, if you put two fingers on the edges, if it bites its lip above; then close the wound, and this is kept if it does not slip, and put in another tweezers afterwards in the same way as before, until the wound is whole; and ligate the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the chief [of the intestine] bursts within, and there is no other nuisance to the patient, and it can be ligated with a fine thread that is cut from the intestine itself, in parts: take the chief of this thread of intestine that is coming out, and then ligate to the chief of this thread one thread of linen twisted, then pass the thread through the needle, and ligate the intestine, and keep it in place; and this method of stitching with tweezers is not fierce but according to the way of fashion and hope; and if the wound is great and wide, just as it is in one of the greater intestines, if there is no other remedy, except for subtility.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	or that it should be excised.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Wounds that open or burst from any wound or incision, when they swell, are called universally 'fistules', and even when they are sewn up and drawn tight.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	A fistula is a swelling that occurs due to a prolonged and painful wound or incision. It is just as if a bird's quill has been driven through the wound; sometimes it is clear and tight, sometimes it is thick and loose. Sometimes it is shallow, sometimes deep; sometimes it is loose, sometimes tight; and I have already mentioned it in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed must have one of these seven causes: that is to say, by the smallness of the wound or the hardness of the tissue; or by its malice; or because there is hard matter inside, and on the skin, that does not allow new matter to grow; or there is too much swelling; or the blood vessels are ruptured, and the matter is of poor quality; or the medicine is not good at curing; or because the corruption is like pestilence; or because the property of the region is late in digestion and in healing, and escapes by nature; or there is a vein or bone involved. And I have already mentioned all these causes and their signs and treatments in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or you must know that I will tell you the cure for fistula, which is done by the work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Wounds that occur in all limbs due to corrosion; for there are wounds that arise from great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or at the jaw, or the intestine, or the bladder, or on some of the ribs, or on the spine, or on any joint of the hands or feet; and if part comes to the property of the main limb, and the rest remain.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	All wounds of this kind are of grievous healing, and there is nothing but toil and ignorance; and if there is no wound that does not reach the very marrow except as I have said, you must have recourse to an attempt to drain or burn it out, if the wound is straight; and if the wound is festering, if you can pluck out the spur with a subtle attempt, for it swells inwards toward the curvature; and if the wound is compound and you do not well bind it, if the moisture is too coarse from one perforation to another, and inflates; then when you know certainly the depth of the wound, whether there is bone or nerve, and that it is firmly grasped, and ask the patient of the pain he feels at the pressure of your hand, and the location; and when you know truly the depth or location, and if it is far from a joint or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the things I have said, if the bandage fits according to what I have said, and if the bone is fractured, and the corruptions that are within; then cure as long as necessary, and if the wound is deeply straight, if you can well bandage it, then put in soft packs until the medicine consumes the superfluous matter that remains; and then apply oily unguents to the surrounding area until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, if you must cauterize as I have said, and if the bone is fractured by the wound, if it is necessary.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or major arteries are not congested, and if the bone is discovered to have corruption and blackness, if the latter extends as far as the whole bone, then cure the surrounding matters while they are sound; and if they are not sound, and return as before, extract the diseased parts until you reach the marrow; and if you reach the marrow and find it sound, then you have cured the disease.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If the disease is too deep to reach, do not attempt to cure it; if there is no other remedy except to leave it as it is; and if there is a small bone that is corrupted, and you attempt to extract it with instruments, if the extraction is made with a suitable instrument, and if there is any remaining bone, do not leave even a fragment; and if moisture opposes you, and there is no doubt or fear, then grasp and moisten and burn, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	If thou dost not well stop them at an hour, put upon the wound something which doth restrain corruption, and leave it until the blood hath clotted round the bones; then it will have less pain. And if it be a great bone, as a leg or thigh, thou must so soon as possible reduce the corruption until the marrow be altogether ossified; then restore the wound. And if there be a great part of the bone corrupted, and blood comes down to the marrow; if thou canst cover it with silk and cover all until the corruption is over, and then cure it until it be healed; and I will tell thee of a fistula which happened to me in my leg, that thou mayest take example and help in thy work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	When I was a youth of about thirty years, I had a pain in my leg from a cause which came from within the bone, until the matters came to the leg, and I had a great abscess which did not have any cause to open; but I left it by my folly to open more than necessary, and it corrupted a great deal of matter, and became a fistula, and there came out so much pus that all the bones were swollen and moist with pus; and I left it like that for two years, and there was no skill in my hands, as I was told, until I was called away, and I saw my leg and the medicines which were being given, and what was causing the pain through the pores of the bone; and it became red all over the leg, and had the color of citrine.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I bound a loop in one of these holes, and then encompassed all the holes, and found that one followed the other throughout the limb.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I thereupon bound one of the holes and found a part of the bone; it was corrupted and black, and the corruption spread to the innermost part of the bone; I removed what appeared to be corrupt bone and thought there was no further corruption, except for what I had seen; and having begun to restore the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, I was unable to bind it; then I began again, and again found the corruption continuing in the bone, and so I removed it, and then I bound it, and I thought I would bind it firmly; but I could not do more than I had bound around a palm of the bone, and I had to remove it entirely, and I restored it with medicines; and it healed and was bound soundly, and did not suffer any further from the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it, or from fear of death which I had avoided for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For often is there bloodletting in the treatment of these cases, but they remain whole; and from the bone there grows a hard scale, and it is in a good state and causes no pain or discomfort in any way, neither to the patient nor to anyone else.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	If the bone is fractured in no part of the limb, if you wish to bind it in this manner: take one thread and stretch it at the head of the bone which is open; command no one to extend it upwards; and put another thread of linen thicker than the first, and bind it above the scale that is coming away from the bone, and extend the head, so that you may tear out the corrupt scale at the bottom, and uncover the scale above the limb or where you see it bound; that the thread does not stain the scale; and put a pledget or a piece of sponge beneath the bone to cover the corrupt scale; and bind as much as you can see and feel the corruption, and bind once more.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted, and is not seen, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, if you uncover the flesh entirely; then put on a pair of gloves and join together the corruption from one part to the other, and be sure to join for the length of the corruption as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, if you join the corrupted joint and join the bone or that which it contains from the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, if there is no other vessel except for the covering; and if the corruption is in the wrist or the elbow, if it is strong in that thing, but always enquire about the corrosion, how it appeared to you; and moderate it in every way that you can, but that the vein or nerve does not hinder you; and that the incision and the sutures cover these bones many times, according to the size of the bones and the appearance of inflammation, and their thickness and thinness, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness. And for this reason it is necessary to perceive a similar resemblance of work in this instrument; and that the work will show you the instrument of which you have need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the methods of diseases; if you suspect the instrument of which you have need according to this.
dou feu	If you think of the instrument which you must use in accordance with what it is intended for, do so with fire.
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The head of the shoulder suffers from swelling or by injury, or by fever; and when you have treated the cause of the swelling with medical means, it does not suffice, if you do not cover that limb up until the swelling subsides; for if the patient escapes by this means of death, or by malice, which is greater, from the fault of the limb; and the sign is that the limb becomes black, as if it were burnt by fire, and afterwards the blackening spreads throughout the limb, taking hold of all the flesh; if you delay covering it, and if it is from the bite of venomous creatures such as scorpions of the sea and vipers and the like, if the infection is at the head of the bone, if you do not give it space to come down to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes down to the hand, if the swelling is at the joint, if the infection does not reach the forearm; and if it comes to the forearm, if the swelling is at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there is no remedy stronger than the quantity of its virtue; and do all that you can when the infection comes or departs: if it comes in the first joint, if you cope afterwards the other joint; and if it comes or departs, if you cope all the way through; and if it comes to the thigh, if you cope at the knee; and if it comes below the knee, if there is nothing else to do but let the patient die; and you should cover or bandage the limb if you tie it up from below and above, and spread one minister over the lower limb and another minister over the upper limb, and you should drain the wound which is between the two limbs at one spatulate wide, until the bone is exposed; then you should cope or drain, and put a bandage part of the way over the drape, so that the infection does not touch the sound limb, and cause the patient further damage and incision.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	If blood flows from a wound while working, if you cauterize the flesh excessively, or put on restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is complete, and then bind the limb firmly with a secure ligature and treat it until it is healed. And I will tell you a story from my home: there was a blackness which seemed to burn with fire, and that corrosion began in the center of the hand, until it consumed the whole hand; and when we saw the corrosion, if we did not cover the hand, it was healed; and long after the corrosion had vanished, it returned again, and I had to amputate the hand. I did not wish to amputate it, for the virtue of the body was weak; and he awoke, returned to his home, and covered his hand, and was healed; and I have never heard of such a thing happening except in this case.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Never comes the abscess in the flesh of the charnut and stays as long as it makes great swelling of the belly; then it bursts and breaks, and in the leap of the belly, it bursts the bowels, just like a vessel; and the skin that is under is just as thin as a veil of thread, and does not reach the bone, neither the nerve, and such an ailment is called "sain," and is not called "fistula"; but if it is so prolonged that it comes down to the bone marrow, it is called "fistula"; and the skin is that if you grasp that skin all around, and even when it is thin, just like a veil; and it does not matter for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	If you see that the skin is swollen and the corruption is not in the marrow, and the skin is thick like flesh, if the surgeon suspects a fistula: look if the swelling is great, and the belly is of a foul odor, then make a clister of Egyptian medicine which is made like this: take alum, oil, and alum stone, equally, and put the skin in a vessel on the fire, until the medicine is red and as thick as honey; then take of this according to your need, and do so hot and cold, and put the medicine on the wound, and hold the opening; leave the medicine in for two hours, then take it out expressing; do this several times, until the swelling is gone and the pain is gone; and never give clister of vinegar, except when this medicine is not present, and take vinegar of figs, and vomit, and then give clister again, until you are sure that the swelling is well healed; and if the patient cannot bear it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the vinegar of vinegar, if the clister is of vinegar and honey or there is a little alum stone broiled; or you give clister of honey and wine mixed, that the honey has the property of soothing and washing, and the wine makes the wound dry; and when you have done this, and you are sure that the swelling is well healed, if the fistula has been cured by this, and you take plaster of Paris, and do so with oil of rose and wine; or you give clister of some medicines and unguents, of which I have spoken of the properties or treating of unguents; and if the opening of the wound is small, and the pain of the fistula will not enter, if you widen with a needle a little, and put in a little unguent of Egyptian or basilicon, as much as it is widened; and if the wound is too wide, if the cuff and the fistula can enter, and if the discharge from the wound is below the level, if the fistula is above or lower than it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bow is in parforce, if you do not leave it to hang loose; and if you do not cover its skin as you see, if it appears in such a manner that the bow goes lower than it should, for when the bow is in parforce, if you do not leave it to hang loose and if you do not cover its skin as you see, if it appears in part: that the bow goes lightly forward, and leaves nothing of the bow; and take solidifying medicines to bring out the blood, and extend over a drape of linen that covers the whole blood; then cover the force of the wound further than before, for there are often sparks on the other drape in proportion to the quantity of the wound, and put it on the wound of the blood to align the bow, and do not remove the great drape except after maintaining for once; and that which comes out of the wound often returns to restore the bow, and its strings that correct the bow, whether from poison or blood or enough, or digested or indigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is swelling or not, and when your medicine is in part manner extended and you see the nature that spurts out of the wound, if its strings have already gone slack, and approach the safety; and then loosen in the morning, or the third day, and when you loosen the wound, if you change the other drape, and renew the spark.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	If the limb hangs limply downwards after the joint has been dislocated, the veins swell up and the blood does not flow properly.</start_of_turn>
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poison comes in a long drawn-out way, if you do not rouse yourself from sickness, for sickness is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	And if subtle poison comes in a long drawn-out way, if you do not rouse yourself from sickness, for sickness is approaching. For there are some who delay their ailments in their wounds, and others do the opposite; and if it persists insatiably, after much time has passed, the veins that are not healed do not swell; and if the veins are delayed in healing, and are stretched, if there is a sudden medicine of drying substances and moist substances, as with diaphoresis, for there is a great part of vitriol in it, which is the last medicine; take diaphoresis and mix it with rose oil and the juice of a vine equal in substance; then confirm and use it. This will cause honey to adhere more firmly, when diaphoresis is not present, or take myrrh, aloes, and incense, grind them, and sprinkle them on honey when it comes out of the fire; and then apply a bandage. de l’aposteme de l’ungle	from the incision of the vein.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises from the swelling of the pouch of the hand, or the heel, or by chance originates in other two places; and when it is inflamed, and care is not taken, if it comes to an abscess of the thumb, it swells and boils until it reaches the root of the thumb, and by chance it swells all the way; and comes the corrosion until the bone, so that there is sharp pain, and the head of the thumb is loosened, and the colour is pale.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés. Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.
