des vils	Des vils.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	The veins are full of black humours which come in greater numbers to the limbs that are bent and move, than to those that are straight.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	You must therefore never give any purgatives, and then the rest of the balsam.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment of iron is in two ways: one is with the forceps, and one is to compress the black blood; or the other method is to ligate the vein and force it out.</start_of_turn>
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The size is as follows: first stretch the limb strongly with lukewarm water, until the great bone is not felt to tremble; then strain the limb of the patient from under the hip joint down to the heel; then ligate the vein in one, or two, or three places, of a large size; then cut and force out the black blood from hand to hand, until as much blood as the patient can tolerate has escaped; and then ligate and command that he abstain from meat eating black bile; and repeat the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and do not do harm to the patient.</start_of_turn

The ailment of this is as follows: open the limb of the patient, if there be hair, then put or bathe it in warm water, and raise the limb until it turns red; and if you have no bath, if the fire is lit, and then place a cover over the vein from the groin to the knee, or from the ankle to the knee; then tighten the leather around the belly, and support the vein from the inside, until it bursts when you feel it; and you will see it red and black, and when it comes out or the leather seems like a white thread; then withdraw the needle from the groin, until it is freed from the leather, and then put a little pressure on it, and put it in another place in the same way; and do this again, or several times if you must; and when you have finished, bring the limb back to its original position, and put another cover on it, just as you did before; then put on another size, or more if necessary; and leave it, and put the thumb on the toe, and keep it there until the second size; and then take out the needle from size to size, until it is gone, and then put it on; and if you do not manage to pull it out and lift it, if there be a splinter at the end of the thread, grasp it and pull, and there will be blood; and hold your hand from one side and the other, until there is none left; and keep that it does not tighten, for if it tightens, you will not be able to pull it out or lift it, and that will be to the disadvantage of the patient; and when you have finished with it, take out the foreign body from the wound and cover it with vinegar and rose oil.

de la voinne civile	of the civil vein.</start_of_turn>
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is enclosed in the arm, in hot parts or where there are no herbs or trees, and in the earth or where there is no moisture; and by chance it is found elsewhere except in the arm, and this comes from the corruption that comes from the decay of the skin, as it comes from the inside of the serpent’s body and outwards, enclosed between the skin and flesh.</start_of_turn
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if there are signs of the beginning of this vein if there comes to the limb a very great inflammation, then it contracts the muscles and the vein bursts like a plant root.

If the vein bursts open, if it is suspected that it has been covered with a piece of sponge from one and a half fists to two and a half, and the thumb, and left for the limb, and every time that there is a point of discharge, if the covering is pulled over the sponge, and the thumb, and if it is too long, if you cut off a part of it and cover the rest, and do not cover the root, until it is entirely expelled; for if you cover it, if it returns to the flesh, it causes embolism and gangrene or death. Therefore, it is necessary that it should be treated immediately and promptly until it is completely cured, without leaving anything or any foreign bodies in it; for in no case has this vein been treated with more than five fingers of sponge, or ten, and one has already seen that it has escaped from ten fingers of length, and when it is covered, there is often one or two cracks or holes, and it bursts to the very bottom; and let out the matter that is within, and bring in healing medicines that will prevent gangrene, then cure it as with an embolism.</start_of_turn>

des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	And never has this vein hands rained, even when it opens at the elbow, or at the wrist, and there comes moisture from the opening; cure it therefore as we have said before.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "buffalo sickness," because it often causes swelling in the buttocks, and is a small vein that grows between skin and flesh, and runs throughout the body, up and down, and is felt quite strongly from limb to limb, until it bursts through the skin or comes out, and spurts blood; and is accompanied by the discharge of various humors, such as bile, worms, and blood clots or pus. And there is doubt of its malice, for when it runs through the body, and ascends to the head, and comes out, by chance it returns and destroys the fat; and this happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it cured and treated, if it cannot be forced out except when it goes out: if you must, then bind the limb above and below with a strong ligature that is tightly secured; then grasp above and pull down, and if it does not come out, if you cauterize the fire above, until it dies; and the greatest harm that it does is when it bursts the oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming or close to the oil, grasp below its nail and pull down, and grasp above, and pull down; and you must use the patient of nourishment of solid medicines for the bad humors carried by the bile, and if he consumes fatty foods.

This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and is a pain that comes in the limbs one after the other; and I saw that which I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I went to see a sick woman, and found her arm swollen, and saw a small swelling in the pit of her elbow; and afterwards, it went up as high as a worm on a pear, more swollen than anything, like silver when it comes out of the furnace; the pain went away from that limb, and settled in the elbow, and then went down to the wrist; then she told me that it twisted back in the limb, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marvelled at how it twisted back and forth between the limbs, for I had never seen such a disease according to this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I do not know whether it is good to move the limb from place to place, but I do not think so, as I saw in the woman; and I thought that it was because the woman had dry bones and exposed veins, and because of that appeared that constraint; and I do not see according to this reason those who have moist bones and veins repaired

Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The bandages are diverse, according to their appearance and according to the nature of the wound or the pain they relieve.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres. Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When she cries out in no limb of these members, and her sign of death, which I will tell you later, learn: if you delay the extraction of this arrow, for there will follow many other complications; and when this is a bad sign, do not learn from me, for the arrow is not withdrawn, but go and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of madness when the arrow cries out and pierces the bone, and leaps the marrow that is above the brain, is when scooping and sooting and vomiting and spitting, and inflammation and redness of the eyes, and spasm and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and by chance there is no bleeding from the nose or ears; or by chance the speech and voice are lost; and leaps from the wound a white moistor resembling pus, and in leaping also as blood-stained hair; and if this sign teaches you, if you are holding out, take out the arrow if it is not firmly embedded.</start_of_turn>
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	When the nipple aches or is pulled, the sign is that it is close to the left breast, and feels as if it were caught in something hard, not soft; and by chance the nipple moves just like a poulp, in dark blood and comes with cold sweat and a cold chill, and fainting: there is doubt that death is imminent.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an infected wound is that never without plains of pus does it pour forth from the wound; the throat swells, the patient's face turns pale, and he breathes heavily and sighs with aversion.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow comes out through the cover of the wound, if it be small, it causes great pain and great swelling and breathing; and all the limb is moved from side to side
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow comes out or is broken within the wound, by chance that it comes out of the wound without any sign of indigestible meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow comes out or is broken within the wound, and in coming out does not pass any feces through the intestine, if there is no hope of recovery, do not attempt to extract the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the stone is in the bladder, and the urine spurts out and comes out forcefully, and the patient feels great pain: the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, if it is like that with the face, the throat, the chest, the armpit, the groin, the shoulder, the elbow, the wrist, and the leg, and the like, is in great distress according to numerous situations.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the stone is in the nerve or the artery, and it is not venomous, as I have said before, for this reason I say that it has happened to me that...
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	In my home there was a woman who was vomiting or spitting up phlegm at the root of her ear: I held her hand, and she bled from the other ear, and was cured without any medicine.</start_of_turn>
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And she bled from an ear during a game of bowls when she choked on oil from the mustard seeds, and the arrow was expelled whole, and did not touch anything except the tip towards the dust, and the arrow was as big as a Turkish bow; and all this happened without any damage to the ear.</start_of_turn
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And take out an arrow from the throat to a crestfallen man, and the Arab arrow was in the ear: I grasped the beard and subtilised as much as I could, and the crestfallen man was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And took out an arrow from a wound, which was in the side or belly, and thought he was dead; but after he had been without movement for thirty days, if he did not recover his composure; I cut on the arrow and extracted it, and pulled it out, without any mishap.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if a man has an arrow stuck in the side or back, and the wound is deep; and when I pulled out the arrow from within, I did not bind up his wound, and he did not feel any discomfort in any of his natural works
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And thus it happened to another man, that he was pierced by an arrow in his face, and the wound was closed; but he continued to suffer great pain; and there were many other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And thus it happened to another man, that he was pierced by an arrow in his face, that it was stuck in the middle of his nose, and was a declining wound to the right side; and the arrow was completely extracted. I was called to treat him after he had been thus for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound very sore.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I tried to treat it with all my skill, and did not feel it; and there was no pain or tingling in his right ear
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrow. I put on the plaster and digestive poultice, so that the wound would not swell; and the arrow came out by itself
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put the thumbs in place again, and closed the wound, and held the patient's hand long tense, until he felt the arrow inside his belly; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put the corrosive medicine on the wound with my thumbs, until it was sufficiently open, and held it, and felt the head of the arrow which was inside the belly; then I closed the wound with the medicine, until the tip of the arrow appeared visibly; and it went well until the third month, and then grew wider so that I had to remove the nails, and I split it in two parts, and could not bear it; for I continued to suspect and tempt it in various ways, until I took away the nails as they were well made, as it is said at the end of this chapter, until I finished with it, and returned the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the doctor judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored: I restored it nevertheless, and the wound was sutured, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or you have spoken of the quality of the extraction of some arrows, if you put your cure on that of which I do not speak, for the books do not teach me that; but you masters know well enough about many great things, and about that which is present and lacking, find nine works, and a new instrument, in descending order of the things which arise in this art.</start_of_turn>
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that the arrows do not emerge from limbs or are ficxed falsely, for they can be managed in two ways: either by force or by hook and loop; and that which leaps forth by the loop or enters, is an arrow pierced through flesh, and leaps no more ever.</start_of_turn
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not move now, let it stay until the chariot is fully borne; and rejoice in its issue; and if it is fixed in the bone and cannot be moved, if you leave it there for some days, and move it every day; then it will move. And if it does not move, if you prick it thoroughly from all around, until the wound is enlarged, and then draw it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the splinter is fixed in the bone of the shoulder, and goes up to one of the bellies of the brain, and some of the things I have mentioned above concerning the patient: if you do not draw it out, but leave it as it is until it is even again after some days, for if the splinter comes up to the surface, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the splinter is not firmly fixed in the bone alone, but comes out only as far as the surface of the skin, and remains in the patient for some days without any mishap, even if the pain recurs.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is firmly stuck and cannot be shifted, if you administer tarteris around, as I have said; then cure the limb until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	If the splinter is seen only in the bone and does not come out further than the surface of the skin, and remains in the patient for some days without any mishap, even if the pain returns. If one sees the splinter, and if it can be grasped without any instrument, and if one does not touch the wound excessively, and for the depth of the splinter, and if there is no bone, nerve or vein in the wound, if the pain is great as in the wound itself; then grasp the splinter and if there is anything holding it in place, break or remove the surrounding tissue as much as possible until it can be grasped; and take care not to break the splinter itself, but to grasp it more firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you do not manage at once, if the limb remains limp at the entrance, grasp it firmly, for its extraction brings relief.</start_of_turn>
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	If blood discharge opposes the remedy, as we have said in this chapter concerning the treatment; then hold off on incision of the nerve and vein. Put in place whatever method you will use to extract the arrow, whether it be toward the heel or the knee, firmly or gently; and keep the patient in the position in which the arrow went in, for that is the greatest aid. If you are unable to do so, follow what the signs tell you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another place, or if there is no wound, or the skin is swollen in the place where it is seen or felt: then leave it in place until the nails can hold it, and then extract it: if it comes out now.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, if you round your hand around it until it goes into the bone, and expand the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be grasped, if you leave it in, and then resume the extraction until it comes out; if the wound is deep, if the arrow has all its force, if the wound is broad and you see the tip of the arrow stuck, if you give it time, if the arrow is grasped by the instrument, so that the tip of the arrow is between the teeth of the instrument; and then pull out, and if the arrow is grasped, if the instrument has a pointed handle entering the wound, to ease the extraction.</start_of_turn
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	If the wound is surrounded by hair, then you must remove all the hair around or the venom is there; if you do so, then cure the wound as it should be cured.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If the wound is near the hair or on the head or the belly or the bladder or the ribs, and it is close by, and you do see it, then cover over it; and keep the vein and nerve covered, and then extract it, and then close the wound, if necessary; and cure it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tweezers used to grasp the splinters is like a bird's beak, and thus is this shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape at the end of the bone is like the quill of a bird, to push out the tip of the wound, as it is in this form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of nails to push and to grasp is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Of common veins there is pain.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are veins which one must know are within, that is to say: two veins which are behind the ears, which are covered by two «herbs»; and two arteries which are in two temples appearing; and two veins which are in the two armpits, which are covered by «spurs»; and the vein which is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein which is at the top of the nose; and two veins which are either in the collar or in the throat; and two veins which are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins which we commonly speak of are five in each arm: one is the cephalic, and is on the left side of the costus, and they call it the lazy vein; and the median is called the fasted, and is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and they call it the brachial vein; and the basilic is either on the left or right side of the costus, and they call it the belly vein, and is above the olecranon, and it is the one which we commonly speak of, which appears openly on the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the saving vein is the one which is between the ulnar and the annular, and if there are two, and in the leg or foot there are three veins: one which is under the elbow of the left costus, and the second which is at the ankle of the right costus; and the vein which is called the great, which is in the ankle of the other costus; and in the other leg there are three veins under those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The blood of the veins that are behind the ears helps to expel old blood and evacuate; and the quality of the blood, as I have said, is that you raise the head of the patient and rub the palm of your hand or the veins are of a rough texture; then stretch the patient's neck with a twist, as long as two veins appear behind the ears in two loops depending on the head: if the patient has a feeling of swelling there, it is an indication of infection; then take the lancet and pierce the vein until it reaches the bone, then keep your hand over the whole vein above, and press and the skin and the vein well two must pass through, and make the blood spurt out until you see; then strain and bind, until it is healed; and I have already said the incision and the cautery or the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The blood of the two arteries that are in the two temples, if it is like an ancient emigration, sode, and obtalmia accustomed, and at the root of the tears of water there are eyes; and the quality of the physician is such as I have said: and that the patient has strained his neck, as the two veins open widely; and he feels the pulse falling down his forearm, and then he signs his mark; then he places his thumb on the vein in the upper part of his forearm, and holds the lancet down, and holds the vein in the upper part, and the cope, as he has done in two other veins, and makes correction of the blood according to his necessity; then he frees the patient, and places his thumb on the vein for an hour, then puts on a bandage; and then the swelling forms, and he leaves it until it is healed; and we have spoken of this and its management and extraction, or the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The blood from the front vein is worth as much as that from the cephalic vein; there are ancient diseases of the face, emigration, and redness; and the quality is that if the patient turns his head while the vein is open, take the instrument which is called the "fosseur", which is like this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	The blood from the front vein is worth as much as that from the cephalic vein; there are ancient diseases of the face, emigration, and redness; and the quality is that if the patient turns his head while the vein is open, take the instrument which is called the "fosseur", which is like this. Place the point on the vein, hold with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow as much as you see fit; then loosen the patient’s neck and ligate the vein until it is firm and never again let the work be done with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not appropriate for me to suggest that the flame should be too strong; and the same with the passage of time, for the bone is close, and by chance the flame breaks when it is thin.</start_of_turn>
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The blood from the two veins that are two fingers wide helps with the swelling, boils, redness, and yellow spots; there are diseases of the face; and the quality is that if the patient turns his head without restraint, as before, then do the same, and let the blood flow freely for a long time with a wide flame, for there is no char.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is subtle, by chance if it breaks; then make an incision of blood, as much as you are able, and then bind up above and below, and hold it firmly.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	When blood from a vein does not flow as it should, and is pale, and has fever, or has been affected by migraine and redness of the face, or is old; and when the quality of the blood is that the patient has tightened his collar, then he should grasp his wrist with his left hand, take a long flame and touch it to the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open easily, and it will not open without some effort; and do not push too much, but correct the blood according to your need, and leave it bound for a night, for it is easily restored. This is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The blood of the two armpits helps to relieve swelling, to initiate mixing, and to cure various diseases, and has the power of antidote against herpes and carbuncles; and the quality of the blood is that when the patient tightens his collar from both sides, as we have said; and whether the master is standing over the patient’s head and the patient sits on one seat, then grasp the vein widely from long, and do the bleeding steadily, or as much as is necessary; then repeat the process in the other arm, then remove the ligature, and gently pull on the middle veins so that the patient is not strangled; and leave it until morning, when the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	From the blood of the leaves.
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins of the arms above helps to cause swelling in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and wounds of the lips, and pain and throbbing.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	When the blood of the leaves is to be taken, command the patient to sit before you, and constrain his neck as I have said; then cut the vein, and observe two veins, one on the right side of the leaf and the other on the left side, and know them by their blackness, and by the fact that they have small black veins running alongside them: cut one and the other, and if you do not know them and are in doubt, if one of the greatest parts of the armpit is cut, and do the same with two veins that are below and above, for this is a safe method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	And from the blood below the tongue.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The blood of the veins below the tongue helps after the blood of the head; and this is at the widening of the throat, and there are diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the physician is that if the patient sweats between his hands before the sun, and he holds the tongue, and looks below on each rib towards the cost, one black vein: cut both of them, but do not go too deep, for below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins which we commonly call healthy are usually sound in two ways: either by puncturing with all the flame of a large fire, or by olive oil if like cuts of trenchers, and is called 'anesil'; and they are large and subtle according to the size and extent of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The flame like a mirror if it is famous, and is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And there is a kind of surgeon who, to open the large veins full of blood that appear, contains great blood and trouble; and this is the form of the olive oil flame
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	It is more subtle and effective, and is useful for smaller veins, or where there is little yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The blood of the basilisk, which is one of these veins, helps to cure ailments such as sore throat, and cough, and pain in the belly; and it is useful for the patient that he should remain calm and that he should abstain from the artery that is causing the disease.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it grasps the bone, and blood flows, if it must remain suspended, as I have said; and must not be plunged into the flame, but cut off as with an anvil.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the bleeding does not stop manifestly, if you must extract it, and bind another; or you wish no more blood, or you prefer to leave in its place the belly in the arm: it will stop manifestly; and grasp the flame with an anvil, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you see that the blood vessel is about to burst, if you must therefore extract the limb, touch the flesh until you know the pulse; then mark the place, and then bind the limb, and grasp the vein with the flame anvil; and beware that you do not cut the artery when you see the limb swell, for this is the artery: stop it immediately.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	If thou seest it swell high up like the urine of a child, and it is neither red nor yellow, know that it is without an artery: haste then, and place thy thumb upon its length, and keep thy thumb still if it is not stained; for it often happens thus; if thou dost lay thy hand upon it, and leave it still, and move not the patient, and be cautious lest he be mad.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	If he is not firmly grasped and you feel pain, and the physician is not present, if the artery bursts open because the head of the retraction has slipped; grasp firmly without delay.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take an embolus of pitch, and make it bleed, and take one half and place it upon it until the other half is reached; if it does not bleed, it is well; if not, if the physician has said so, apply powders that stop bleeding; for the clotting of blood is not firmly fixed in many situations by the small size of the wound, and the power of the hand.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The blood of the vein in the middle helps to cure blood clots at the root of the head and the bones below, because it is composed of the basilar and cephalic veins, as we have said; and it is recommended that the patient should cause the nerve below to swell, and if it does not swell too much, and if it finds the nerve, it swells and the blood clots either disappear or are cured; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in some people because of its subtlety, it is recommended that you take the blood from the anesic instrument; and remove the nerve from your sight.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	If there is a vein between the two nerves, and it is felt to be long
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The blood of the cephalic vein helps to cure blood clots at the root of the head, and helps to stop the bleeding; and it is recommended to cauterize with the olive flame or the myrtle flame, for this is the most effective of all veins, because it has neither nerve nor artery
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Whatever, one must ask more gently at first, and grieve nothing if it does not succeed the first time; and by chance it swells up again among some people, one must do it the first time, but one grieve nothing.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your opinion.</start_of_turn>
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about health is that when blood is drawn, it must only be for the preservation of health and to ward off future diseases; and it must be taken from one of the three veins which are or should be used: namely, the cephalic, the facial, and the basilar; and it must be done at the beginning of prayer, fasting, and eating, when the sign of repletion appears; and it must be drawn either in the morning or in the evening, after two or three hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The blood which is drawn for diseases has no fixed time, but whenever there is a need for a cure or treatment at any time and in any condition; and one must not draw blood from children until they are twelve years old, nor from women for more than four months until they are seven months pregnant
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Blood should not be given to those who have passed 60 years.</start_of_turn>
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	When anyone feels well, in whatever way, if it comes to his bowels, if there is a slight retention of wind, so that the veins do not draw out the humors from the principal parts; do not let him eat too much flesh, neither too little, for it is better to be moderate; do not give him dropsy, vinegar or urine; and if he vomits after eating, and has a sore belly, and many loose stools, and excessive weeping, and sleeplessness, and this with any other vice, or by some weapon or poison; then subtilize the humors, not when they are large, but by diet and drink and medicine, if you can; and give him either a cold or warm bath, for nothing must be left untended; and let him lie down with his head somewhat higher than his heels, and stroke his arm twice or thrice, then remove the thread from the middle; for if it is too tight or loose, it will not hold; then stroke the limb with your hands, until the veins swell up and you feel them; then moisten the patient with a spoonful of old oil, then place his hand over that vein which is below the elbow, for a moment or two, until he feels well.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flee like strings to the physician, and if there are some that are full of windiness, so that when one puts on the flame, it shrinks away from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus it is with these; and if it opens the vein, it is too wide, because of this it is that the physician must be advised in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein swells the first time, that is good; if not, one must repeat the process several times until the swelling subsides.</start_of_turn
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	If the limb is inflamed and the patient hopes for the wound to heal by itself, and leaves it for a year or two, without supporting the arm: by chance there will be abscesses; do not enter or bathe, then restart the bleeding if it stops; if it is a small wound, or without a clear sign that there is less blood than you saw, even if you burn the wound directly; and that work is done without delay, even if the limb is inflamed; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If thou seest the limb inflamed, if thou dost not wish to renew the blood, put upon a little ball of lint soaked in oil, for it doth soften the hard parts of blood; and it doth harden in this limb the lint that is oiled; and thus administer the oiled lint into the wound that thou dost bleed the veins, to stop the course of blood; and this doth cause a tingling and swelling of the parts, when it is put upon the limb; if thou takest it off too soon and it is too great.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes a great abscess which has often happened, even though it is not sick only at this time or the opening of the vein is little, if thou art hasty, put upon the limb a wet sponge and a little gauze, and strain for an hour; and know that thou shalt do this after the evacuation of blood from the vein, and if it remains in the limb after a few days no black or green mark, if thou dost not see it; and if thou seest, put upon no other thing of aloes or mastic gum dispensed in the juice of calamus, mustard, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there has been a burst of wind and the appearance of blood from the basilisk: put your hand on it, and if you find the limb soft under the compression of the hand, if that is the bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Leave off all that we have said, for in court without an artery; but it makes.i. the wound dry by pressing firmly, then treat with another remedy, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	Treat each wound according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the wound.</start_of_turn>
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if it is black, leave it to fester as long as it is red; and if you see it large, leave it until it is slight; and if it is too thick, leave it cool.</start_of_turn
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is fitting for the one who is blunt and strong, and has the skill of extracting blood, to make the wound larger; and let the flame be large; and for the one who is weak, do the opposite, and make it sounder rather than deeper, and must make it sounder by cutting across, not by piercing. And this method of bleeding saves the blood from decay and damage of nerves, and is worth more than the blood that comes from a long cut.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for the one who has a cough that needs bleeding, it is fitting to give soft bread soaked in the juice of green pomegranates; if he is choked, let him spit out blood three times or four. And if he is of a cold complexion, let him chew before the bleeding soft bread soaked in honeyed oil, or in scented honey with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and fragrant oil.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he vomits blood after the evacuation of blood, it is certain that he will spit frothy vomit, and fragrant mucus, and use other things that we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of the stomach.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if it seems to swell up the arm again, and is cured another time, if it is again stained with great blood, it must be bound up and bandaged, according to the quantity of its continuous virtue.</start_of_turn
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who seems to swell up the arm after the first bleeding, and has strong pain, if it is bound up .iii. hours after the first bleeding, or after the twelfth hour.</start_of_turn>
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who appears to be healthier from another side, if he must recover alone in the second hour or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is blood in the belly which is already swollen, and causes fever; if it is certain to expel a great quantity, and expand the belly until it cries out for help; then that you reward all the conditions of blood, and put your hand on the pulse when it is well, that the blood does not come out instead of the vomit, and this often happens when the patient is negligent; and do not do anything except you see the arm slip, and make the vomit again the second time, and the belly is closed, that you press firmly; if it is crooked, extend the arm as far as possible, for that would be bad; but leave it as it is until the second time; or you touch the tip of the flame, until the one who is frozen at the belly's edge has vomited from the stomach, and put a little water on it, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has fled, if you leave it and do not bind it tight, as long as the incision is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if treatment is needed again, if the same vein is in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is healthy in place of the vein of the head because it is composed of this.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And if the patient has a wound in the hand with hot water, until the swelling is red; then bind it moderately, so that the wound opens well; then pull out the wound, do not make it wide or long; or make a large opening, and bring the skin close to the wrist joint, and if that is not enough, if you pull the hand out once more, let the blood drain out naturally until you have enough; and if that is the case, do not pull the hand out with the hot water again, for one puts more into it than in the case; the blood of this vein is more precious than all the veins, for there is neither artery nor nerve in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The blood of the salivary vein of the right hand is worth for all the diseases of the liver, and this is the method: strain the hand and put it in hot water, until the swelling comes out if one sees it; and if the wound comes out, and if you manage to pull it out whole, do not grieve anything; and do not go too deep, for the nerves are all stripped of flesh, and then pull the hand out in hot water, if it is not frozen in the wound, and cannot be pulled out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	When you have treated the blood as much as you can, if you put oil on the wound and bandage it firmly, and do so for every wound.</start_of_turn>
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The blood in the left hand is worth the disease of mice; do everything as I have told you about before.</start_of_turn
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The blood of the sophene is valuable for all diseases that are caused by a weakening of the body, such as diseases of the marrow, retention of flowers, disease of the reins, and of the knees and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its blood is such that when the patient has a cold limb in hot water, and wipes over the belly until it turns pale, and lies down on the joint of the limb; and if the limb is at the ankle, and from under the limb comes out drops of urine; such a wound is either of small or large size, or at the ankle, for the urine is valuable.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you see it on the bone, beware of the nerves that are around it, and handle it just as if you were cutting; and let the flame be calm.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if you cannot move it without pain, if you return the bone to its place in the acute phase, and let the vein drain well.</start_of_turn>
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the urine must be expressed for the first time, if it begins again later on under a little thrust, for the urine is salty; do not doubt, as we have said, and do the same with the other limb equally
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The flesh of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of the foot, and its blood is worth the pain of the groin, when it is full of blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And if the patient is sitting or bathing and the wound is strained upwards of the ankle three times, for otherwise it does not open; and if it opens, do so in every way that you can, and through and through; it is better to leave it closed, for the pus is thick and it will be discharged by itself with the hands of a layman.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	If you do not find any discharge of blood from it which opens or drains downwards, or to the little toe, and you keep it warm; take so much blood from the patient as you see fit, and then ligate the vessel, and put on a bandage and strain; it is now healed.</start_of_turn>
des sainies de ventouse	of the ventouse's bloodletting
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Vacuum is made of horn, or spider, or gut; and is performed in various ways: either by cutting and drawing out blood, or by cutting alone.</start_of_turn>
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this bloodletting by ventouse is done in two ways: either it is done with great heat or with cold; and the bloodletting which is done by cutting and extracting blood is done in twelve pulses, of which one is at the top of the head; and the other is at the root; and two at the two costal cartilages; and the ventouse is on the chin; and the ventouse is on the two scapulae; and the ventouse is on the crura; and the ventouses are on the two arms; and the ventouses are on the two legs; and the ventouses are on the two ankles; and the bloodletting does not affect any great veins that are scattered in the belly, for in this case it would be harmful, as we do when we take blood from a vein; and it is not recommended except when it is administered, neither with great heat nor with cold, in any illness which comes from repletion, until all the stones are evacuated.</start_of_turn>
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if need be for illness compels, or through custom, if the attendants come too close at the commencement of the month, or at its end, and make a commotion and every sort of uproar; for there are some who, when they must make a commotion, become very heavy-headed; and there are some who find swelling and redness on their face, head, and neck, and dark circles under their eyes; and there are some who find a drop of blood in their mouth, have lost their tongue, and spit blood; and there are some who dream and see various things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and indeed when it is necessary because of great pain, we command that the patient be fanned for two hours after
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The blood of the physician helps with the headache … that comes from these dark circles; and it must not be done until all the humours have been evacuated; for this vomiting is in lieu of the cephalic blood, and must only be used for those who have a cold complexion or who are prone to vomiting, for this causes them great discomfort; and for this reason it must only be used in those who are suffering from severe illnesses.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	and if it becomes obvious, it must be placed further down the throat due to the risk of choking.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The wind's action at the collar is in lieu of blood from the head and the brain; therefore it is worth the stretching out of the beard, the splitting of the channel of the tonsils, and everything else, and swelling; and it is likely to burst, because if it stays too firmly, it may cause fainting or vomiting or pain.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The wind's swelling at the collar is worth as much as the pains of the head, and fainting and vomiting, and strangulation, and toothache; and it is in lieu of the blood of the brain; and it is likely that you must order the patient to express his hand to put it [on the wound], that he does not cut the artery, and does not suffer any discharge of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The winds of the south blow low and mild if there is a disease of the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the blood of the upper teeth.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The winds of the spaces are worth a disease that comes from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The wind's swelling at the armpits is worth as much as three veins of the arm, because it draws blood from these large veins; and order the patient not to fill them too tightly, because the limb is subject to fat, and knows nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The swelling which is on the buttocks is worth as many wounds as the roots of the foundation, and has diseases of its own, and it is convenient that the swelling be large and tough, that it has a good hold; and by chance, if it should be small, if it breaks, it makes great wounds.</start_of_turn
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.
