The wounds of the limbs swell widely open, for they attract blood from every part of the body, and are worth as old pains of rain, mud, and bladder, and cause to swell the flowers; and are in lieu of the groin, and the buttocks, and all of them make the body limp after a long usage, and cause vomiting in various positions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the suction is that you put it on immediately, and with a little temperateness, and put it firmly, and move it equally, and do not cease doing so until you see the flesh red and swollen, and open up the color of blood; then withdraw, and put the suction back on, and take care of the body, for there are some who have very tough veins, and clear pores: if you cut once alone, you must make large wounds, and a wound deep; and do it gently
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if it is not big, if you must cut twice: the first time to soften the large blood vessel.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if it is not very thick, if you must do it three times; and when our wounds draw blood too much and too little, if we suffer only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	If our veins bleed excessively, if we rejoin them often; if the wound is not expected to heal, if it is severe, and if it persists even when the cause of the wound has vanished, and it befalls one with thick skin and hard, and with many pores, that you order the application of an aperitif and dissolving oil, such as oil of violet, or sweet almond oil, or oil of pumpkin seed; or if it be in the summer, oil of thyme, or sage, or chamomile, or the like.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the swelling is large and cold, if take bitter oil, or balsam, or oil of rue, and the like.</start_of_turn>
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	If the wound has a tender base and large pores, oil must not be applied, but it is permitted to wash after the evacuation of rose water, or cold water, or vinegar of roses, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or the like.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has moisture in his mouth, if he rises easily, or of hawthorn, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have excessive superabundance of humours shall rise from wine old, or from seawater, or from decoction of rue or chamomile, or from other similar things; and must not use the ventouse before the bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and must not sleep after the ventosation, but must rise when he is due to rise and when he is risen.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And guard those who grow pale are bilious, and if they are too much so and inflamed; if it is to be known that they should take cold things, as with pomegranate seeds and radishes and lettuce easily, and similar things; and eat barley meal, and broth of chick peas, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion, if they take honey syrup, and scented wine middle, which is between old and new, and eat barley gruel, and eat barley meal and small oilseeds and herbs; and when he has ventosated, he must drink more than eat; and it is not permitted for anyone to take garlic or mustard before or after the ventosation, to comfort the principal members; and let it be understood that this must be done discreetly, but it must not be omitted that those who drink the most should also give.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The wounds which are made to bleed are those which are made upon the liver, and upon the spleen, and podagre, and upon the belly and the belly-button and the intestines and the hip, for no member suffers wounds upon its bones, and it is done only to draw blood from one member to another, as we do upon the nails when we do not wish to bleed; to remove the viscosity which is in the member, as we do when we put on a dressing upon the belly and the belly-button to soften the member; and to stop the pain, when there is inflammation or a fracture, for it attracts by its attractive power the inflammation, or evacuates the fracture from its place; and so it makes swell when we put it upon the liver and the spleen when there is retained moisture, and these dressings are administered empty without any liquid, and never are they administered together with water, and never are they plain with cold water, as in diseases of the pleura, and in such a manner we fill the dressing with warm water or with water or with herbs which cover this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the compress administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And there shall be two large and half palms of barley, or eight costers of lentils, a thousand small holes, as though to pierce an arrow; or from thorns, sulfur before if it does not please the patient to put it on the limb; and in the middle there shall be a twig of thorn or iron, to hold the bandage, and there shall be great and small according to the diseases and the hardness of those who take them; for the blisters of the sick are other than fat, and leaner than fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And must one place this sponge on the limb: grasp the bandage with wax or linen, and put it into the sponge through the twig which is in the sponge, so that it sticks either at the bottom of the sponge that it does not burn the patient; and then put it on the limb, and there must be either on the hole that we have said, so that when we look, if it goes up, we take off the sponge; and grasp the linen as before, and repeat often, if you must.</start_of_turn>
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	When the pleural dressing is administered in the treatment of pneumonia, at all its sharpness, there is no point of hardness or rupture, and it is only administered when it is firm; and it is placed upon the limb only so slightly. And this is its form.
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	They are not administered for any other limb where we cannot put a dressing because of its smallness, such as the liver and the spleen, and the like; and when the skin is stripped of hair, such as on the groin or the armpits, and other like; and the quality of the wound if it is that when you find wounds that are in soft and clean blood without any purulent discharge, if they are taken; and put on a little bandage of soft water, until they are familiar, and have nothing in their belly; and then either drain the abscess and dressing, or wipe the limb until it is red, and put on the dressing; and when they are full, and groan, if it is possible to put on a dressing, put it on, for it is worth more after.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If this is not the case, if you lift the limb easily, then later with pain, move it well, and then release it; and if the limb remains too long in the wound, if there is too much blood, put on a cloth of linen in cold water and put it on, until the wound is stretched out; and if the wound is multiplied, put on broken glass or lead, and similar things, until it is stretched out; or take out half of the bones of the limb, and leave them until they burn out, if you have stopped now; and if you have done more mischief, take other bones.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	If the wound does not take hold, wipe the limb with fresh blood, or pierce it with a needle until the wound stops bleeding, and then put on a bandage, and hold it as tightly as it feels comfortable; and when you see that it bleeds again, sprinkle over some aloes and hempseed, or charcoal, if they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	And thus begins the book of bruises.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is the restoration of a bruise and its evacuation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Hear now, dear son, for in this chapter the learned physician reveals things which no ancient book or lettered work has ever mentioned; and for this reason it is strange in our land, for I have never found anything like it; and I know of nothing save by the wisdom of the old books, or through study and experience, or by the customs of my life; and I have set forth in this chapter what is contained therein, and I have abridged it at the end, and I have made clear the forms of the instruments which are mentioned, as I have done in the two preceding chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say or write in the prologue of this book what the words and chapters contain, and that we confirm the truth, so that those who are learned and who are studying this noble art can learn and teach others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twisting or swelling comes to any limb, if you command the patient to hasten the healing of the ailment from one side and the other, if nothing else hinders, if weakness of the limb, or youth or old age; or if the tension is not very strong, or too cold; and eat cold broth, that is to say, cold broth and broth of oil and herbs, and do not drink wine, do not eat any fatty foods, and do not fill the veins with blood too much, until you are certain that the ailment has ceased to progress.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to restore, if you must nourish the patient with foods that cause great swelling, or if there is viscosity, such as barley in water, broth, fish, eggs, cheese, turnips, cabbage, and similar things.</start_of_turn>
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For at the least some relief, the muscles relax and the swelling lessens.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that bones broken in various parts do not mend well nor unite according to their nature because of the moisture in the limbs; neither those that are too tender, like bones of small children; but there is no cure, so maintain above the broken bone the great tension that has appeared and unite the limb together, as much as it strengthens if it were before; and do not move it from its place, for because of this it is necessary to nourish the large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that breaks are of various kinds in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go to the marrow, and others by cutting, as with the size of a pen to write.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a small fissure.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And sometimes there is its own sign and its own instrument in restoration; according to what is remembered from its place; and it is known that the break of the bone is recognized by its turning, and opens well by pushing, and by the pressure of the hand; and when there is no twisting or pressure, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no break; but it can well have twisting, or fissure, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is only possible for me to move the hand slightly, but put on medicines that come afterwards, and then hold it firmly now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And the wounds that break through that go downwards, and are the two parts of the joint, it is necessary to put them right equally, even as after amputation; and if the amputation is close to life, if you leave any spur, as long as the amputation is quiet; then put it right alongside the muscle as you can lightly and cautiously, and the wounds that restore the limb are lighter than the restoration of this or that which has pieces. Then tighten, as it is said above.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if there are broken pieces in the bone, if they extend from two parts, as in the hands or feet, or at the thumb if it is a small limb, or in two strings or in one string and the thumb; and set the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the broken parts of the limb are loosened, if you rejoin them firmly at their place on the muscle that you can, and keep that in your work does not cause the patient pain or injury; and adjust well the two ends of the bone according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And if he feels well in the hand, even though it may seem that it is not well: if the swelling is good and does not tighten too much, do not press too hard as some people do when they are working excessively; for in this way many have come to harm.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is at a joint, if the patient is very sick and does not move it, neither awake nor asleep, neither by day nor by night; keep the limb so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it feels no pain, if it is not at a joint, and you can put it into use without feeling pain; keep it straight, so that no spasm arises until it is restored; and the quality of the limb is as I have told you
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	His limbs are diverse in small and large sizes and shapes.</start_of_turn
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small members, such as arms and thighs and fingers: if you can wrap them with soft and subtle cloths; and those that are large, such as hips and legs: if you can wrap them with a wide and strong cord, for the large cords embrace the whole great limb, and strain it from all sides equally, so that there is no tension; then I will make light dressings, three turns or four according to the limb, and I will strain the hand once for the whole cord, and I will go up to the break and strain less, than the break then comes out a little; and I will soften the cord a little and a little, as long as I take a large part of the limb back, then I will take another cord, and I will twist the dressing back in place above the break; then I will put on the dressing below the break, and I will strain moderately, not too strong not too weak, as we have said at the first hour above; then I will put in between the cords dressings of linen or cloths, until they are even all around, and then I will tie everything up above with a good knot, and then I will put on your supports well made, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or abscess, if you put on something soothing for the abscess, and which will stop the swelling, and leave it for a few days; then strain over your ribs, and let them be half of a broad cane in size, or of mustard seeds, or of gum resin, and be like this figure.
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the rib which you put on the fracture be thicker and wider than the others; and be as long as it is convenient for the limb in its entirety or in its diminution; then strain over the ribs in the same way as before, and then bind under a thread smoothly, as in the first instance on the fracture; the tighter it is bound, the less; and it is necessary that the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, and be of linen wool. For if the thread is thick, like those fools who make their stitches of linen thread, and it is great error, because the stitch will not be even if it is too fine, and it will not hold firmly.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	If the patient is bruised by the nails after the stretching of the flesh, if you put on them stockings of linen or coarse cloth, so that they do not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a burn, and the bone is fractured, I will speak of the cure of that afterwards.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And as regards those who cannot endure the pain of the stars, they must break their limbs at the first opportunity.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	When the limb is large, it is not permissible for me to put these stars in place except after five days or seven, or more according to your certainty of the afterbirth of the caulking; and when this is done the method of ancient embalmings is to restore fracture, dislocation, and torsion: take flour that is held against the walls of the mill, and mix it with abundant eggs, and make this confection, not too clear not too thick, and use it. This is the common method of embalmment that restores the fracture in various positions, and the same for women and young children, for it is neither too harsh nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of dressing that restores the fracture and dislocation and torsion: take three barley grains and linseed and almond and asafoetida and gum arabic and mugwort, in the quantity of x. three; myrrh and aloes, in the quantity of v. three; beeswax . viiij. three; and grind them up, and mix them with plenty of eggs; if the complexion of the patient is hot, use this dressing, for it is of good composition and immediately restores the broken bones, and is worth more than many homes.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of embalmment that is worth for torsion: take mugwort and mastic, mix with X grains of rue; myrrh and aloes, mix with VIIII grains of rue; acacia with VI grains of rue; arnica with X grains of rue, grind them well, and mix with water or abundant eggs, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Other methods of restoring joints and bones that have slipped out of place, relieve pain that arises, and reduce swelling of the bone, and the fracture: take fresh linen, moisten it in oil and put it on the area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These methods do not restore them immediately, but they are good for relieving after-pain and restoring bones properly, relieving pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of supporting the displaced bone is to take dried fig leaves and terrestrial pavol leaves, and grind them together, and make plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Other methods of restoring the fracture and reducing the remaining after-pain.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of viper’s bane, chamomile, violets, fennel seeds, and rue a few parts; grind them up, and mix with wine, and if the limb is swollen, mix with vinegar of coriander or plain vinegar, and use it
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Other methods of replacement are more forceful than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take root of chamomile, flaxseed, balsam, melilot, and chamomile, of all an equal part; and bruise, and confit with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras says in his book that there is no need to put anything on the broken limb to restore it except some wax and oil, and nothing else, and that it should be between soft and hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen would have you put something warm upon the broken limb, to restore, such as mustard, aloes, incense and other things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of dressing that is worth for pain and swelling: take mugwort and chopped onions, or poppy seeds, and vinegar, and mix them evenly, and grind them, and make a poultice of it and bind it.</start_of_turn>
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then loosen a little afterwards, and take care that the patient feels no pain, that the bone is not displaced from its place; if you do not loosen by hand for a while. And if pain comes to the limb, or swelling, order rest or inflammation, if you hurry, and loosen, and support the displacement now; and take a light bandage, and a wet sponge, and immerse in water, and lift the limb, until the swelling stops, and the pain is calmed; then leave the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, soaked in water or oil of rose, and bind up with a nut, until you are sure of the abscess being cured; and rest the inflammation of the limb, and be sure the pain is gone, then repeat the binding, and a little displacement, and do not strain it so much as before; and be discreet until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that swelling, redness, pain and swelling are present throughout the bone, and that you must place and bind, if it starts again, as you did the first time.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If it does not come from the limb nothing of what we have said; if it does not slip from the third day or the fourth or the fifth or the seventh; do not leave it for twenty days, as we see, until the swelling has subsided and the limb has become flexible; then tighten the restraint more than before, and swell the flesh, as I have said previously; and if you see the limb drying out more than usual, the stitches will not hold; then rise up the warm water and loosen the limb every third hour, cutting a little piece of the ligature; by this means the swelling will gradually subside from the limb and restore the limb naturally: that is bad, and if it is a dangerous thing, I do not see anything better than to leave it alone and do it directly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	from various methods of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many kinds of fractures are known, and various figures, and their causes are diverse; for there are fractures caused by percussion of a spear, and the collarbone broken right up to the syphus which is split by the bone, as is often done by a hack or thrust; and for this reason this kind of fracture is called a «hack fracture».
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	For the spear pierces the bone in an opposite direction to that of percussion, and this kind of fracture is called an «absolue»; and there are wounds of these two kinds of fractures, great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded percussion, or fracture or fracture of the bone, or dislocation of the shoulder or fracture of the bone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	If there is a fracture with the bone protruding through the skin, which approaches the socket which is below the bone, or it is on the bone itself, and is this wound, large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if a wound that has penetrated the bone is as slight as a nail, and the fracture is small, this is called a «capillary fracture»; and if the wound is made by a wound of stone, or by thorn, or by anything similar, and causes the bone to split inwards, and the bone is bowed as when coals are placed over a cauldron; if between the fragments.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And in these cases there are more bones that are soft or moist, as in the case of a child; and in all these kinds of fractures, small pieces are loosened if these bones are flexible; and I will speak of them later.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know of all kinds of breaks by the swelling above them, by inquiry, and by corrupt flesh above.</start_of_turn>
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary mark is known by this that when one discovers the bone and rubs it in grease, if the fracture is black.</start_of_turn
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fracture, take heed of any sudden accidents with the patient, and if you see no other mishap, if vomiting of bile, loss of consciousness, extension, swelling, palmation, and fever arise, and the eyes are itchy and flushed, and other similar things besides, do not proceed without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any impending mishap, and you hope for recovery, if so, begin the treatment.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the limb comes first to you, and it is in fever, if so, you must remove the bone before the fourteenth hour of the day before sunset.</start_of_turn
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in this state, if you hasten to open the bone before the seventh hour, even though the marrow is corrupted, there will come the accident we mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if a bone breaks and reaches the edge of the skull that covers the brain, if you know how, you must split the fractured part in two: take hold of the patient’s head and uncover the bone in every way you can, and on the figure of the wound more so; and if blood vessels break out from uncovering the bone, or an abscess, if you can, use what is necessary, and fill the cavity with soaked linen cloths soaked in rose oil; and rest the wound until the abscesses have subsided, and be sure to check for blood vessel damage; then begin to bind up the bone, which is done in two ways: one way if the fracture is close to the tail end, and the other way if the fracture is close to the head end.
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then the other cut is larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that if you have different sizes of nails, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed and of iron; and in order to work lightly, do not split the head
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is tough and hard, if you must pierce through, even if you administer a large dose of medicine, do not make a hole wider than the diameter of the bone; and must have above the tip a margin or circle, which must not pass beyond the bone; and you must have several of these margins, so that the bone comes out from under the thickness of the bone, as with a large dose of medicine; and this is the form of the two methods of administering medicine:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	If the bone is tough and hard, if you must pierce through, even if you administer a large dose of medicine, do not make a hole wider than the diameter of the bone; and must have above the tip a margin or circle, which must not pass beyond the bone; and you must have several of these margins, so that the bone comes out from under the thickness of the bone, as with a large dose of medicine.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have set the bone, and treated it, if you can, reset the fragment that remains detached from the bone with any instrument resembling a chisel, but it must be more rigid and subtle than the other chisel; and if nothing remains of the small bones, do not remove the fragments, even if they are loosely attached to other instruments; then cure the wound with sutures and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of work is that which the Greeks teach, which is more numerous; and the load is very great, and that is its word.</start_of_turn>
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to uncover a part of the bone, either the socket or the fracture edge, so that when you have uncovered that part, if you put some oil on the tip of this incisor lens, from which this is the form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not grasp from one side, but take hold of the limb at two costs; if you grasp from the bone, then immediately release your hold from above, and take hold with a slight mallet from below, so that you can easily move the bone without injuring the surrounding tissue; if it is near the bone, grasp it lightly, for it is easily bruised, because it is well known that it is painful.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the bone breaks without piercing the skin, and the bone is only slightly fractured by its base, and there are small pieces, if it is possible to return the asperity, and to remove the scales with a scraper of various sizes, in order to fill each cavity as completely as possible, according to the work and the figure of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If there is still before great pain, and afterwards more subtle, and does not cease to do so until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In some other surgical procedures and incisions, it is necessary to cause a wound according to the situation; and this is something that is not easily learned by anyone who has not studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	If the swelling is discovered, then you must take hold of one drape of linen, according to the size of the wound, and soak it in oil rose and place it on the wound; then take another drape of linen doubled in two or three, and soak it in wine and oil rose, and place it on the first drape; and do this more gently than you would like, that you do not damage the swelling, and then administer above it another linen, and do not bind it more tightly than is necessary to hold the wound only; and leave it in place for one or two days, until the swelling has subsided, then remove it, and administer medicines such as radish root, flour of times, and incense powder, and an astringent; and from these things make a powder and apply it to the wound, and administer appropriate medicines without biting; and keep the wound clean, do not leave it bloody, do not leave it bound up tightly, for when it is bound up tightly on the swelling, it contracts and causes pain, and this brings great harm to the patient; for when anything biting is placed on the swelling, if it is not done cautiously.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore take heed, if no other misfortune comes to the patient, as we have said, if there is any doubt with regard to it.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If black bile does not depart violently except by the medicine we have placed, that some virtue has, if you take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and in glue one drape, and you put it on the surface; then you will cure in the manner of cures that it is possible, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Never break the three upper parts or one alone, for these are three bones; and since these are cartilaginous and do not break, except by excessive bowing or twisting, they will heal quickly.</start_of_turn>
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	If one of the two parts is broken, if you can swallow your little toe or pierce the knot of pain that you do not want, and put the same break inside your index finger, and at the knuckle by force, until the pain disappears according to its natural figure; and do this gently, and beware that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the upper part and cannot be brought down, if you can, put it equal to the chief of a strong bone
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If the break is of two parts, do it again; and hurry to restore the first joint if you can; if not, after the seventh or eighth day, when the inflammation of the wound has subsided, then bathe the head of the pain where you attempt to bandage it, if the break is in a part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	If not, after the seventh or eighth hour, when the swelling of the wound has subsided, then pourtre at the head of the wound a drape of linen, if the break has occurred in a part. Or you may bite [the wound] once more elsewhere, if the break has happened there; and let the stitches be so large that they fill the hole at the wound's head.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say no restorer must keep the tents moist in the burrow, and die each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I do not see that it is good, but it is necessary that they be moist in the making of an egg and flour powder; then leave the tent until the bone is firm, and the cartilages hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never must one or the other pluck a goose feather in place of stitches, and if indeed there is a soft drape over, and the pincer is held, and the patient is blown among; do whatever you like.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if the patient sweats profusely while working, if one puts some cerote or cotton soaked in rose oil, or in some vinegar.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound does not bleed, if you put on a plaster of alum, of hempseed flour, and of incense powder, confirmed with egg yolk, then put on soft dressings, and do not bind tightly; and if the break is small and is broken into small pieces, if you have suitable instruments, then close the wound, and cure the things that are surrounding it with char, and solder, as with plasters and ointments that are suitable for this; and if there is no wound in the inside, if you cure the tents, and put on bandages of wool, until it is healed
de la routure de la mandibule	of the jawbone.
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is dislocated forward, and there is no wound, the fracture is only superficial, and is not broken in depth, except for spurs within, if one knows it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the outer part, to bite down firmly with the index finger of the affected hand; and if the fracture is on the left jaw, take hold of the index finger of the right hand, and grasp the fracture lightly, and hold it steady with the other hand outwards, and keep it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is displaced inwards, if it is necessary, to administer extension inwards, as much as it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	If movement of the jaw comes loose, or if it is strained by a thread of gold or silver or silk, then put on a broken jaw-bone cerate and put on an i. double drape; and put on the drape a large staple well made, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the jaw, and bind it on to the tooth that you put, and command the patient to rest, and eat soft food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	If you see that the figure is stiff, if it is dislocated from the jaw, and then reset it to its place; and put on a plaster, of powdered mulberry with abundance of eggs or flour of alum, after this has ossified the cerate; and put on the plaster linen legier, and if the plaster has hardened, and the patient’s figure does not stiffen, leave it as it is until it is healed; many times it is healed in two weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if post-partum vomiting comes, if we remember what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, heal without damaging any part of the bone; if subtle from the bone, cover with suitable instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	If the wound is tight, if it has flared up according to your need.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have sutured all these pieces, and there is no longer any pain, if the wound is large, put on suitable bandages to protect the wound, as long as it is healing.</start_of_turn>
de la forcele	forcefully
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forcele breaks several times before, over the shoulder, and breaks if done in two manners: when it is broken and loosened in three pieces, and there are fragments, and it is the lightest to restore; or when there is a break with injury.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And if the break is in the direction of the wound, you must have two assistants, one to hold the shoulder that feels the forcele broken; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then put the break even with the shoulder, so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor tremor.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you must extend more, if put on the shoulder of the patient a round ball of beeswax, or linen, and be large as you need; and extend and hold the forcele, and strain the sphere in your hand, so that you put the break even, as it should be.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you are unable to manage the head of the shoulder when it comes out of its place, because it is coming out with force, you must know that the patient lies prone upon his bed, and place an elbow support, that is, an elbow resting on the middle of the forearm, and hold the minister of the elbow below, until the bone of the shoulder is raised up.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then address the fracture to your side, and if you find debris, if you know it, make an incision there; and force out the pieces gently, and if the bone does not unite by any means, if the socket is at one of the incisors you have; but that you place an elbow support upon the shoulder, to hold the blood clot.</start_of_turn>
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it seems like a scoop, but it is not quite so, and let it be as wide as it seems convenient, according to the size of the bone and the nature of the work; and there shall be two nails, as you see, and one shall be large, and the other small, as is the curve of the wound that you made when you treated the bone; and when you are assured of the postulation, if the wound is slight, or if you doubt the postulation, if you employ the wound with patches and sutures, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if the abscess comes again, if it is moist, then apply oil of roses, rue and wine, and put on top.</start_of_turn>
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The stripping of the bone, when it is sensible to wounds and to the saw, is that you put upon the bone the plaster of fine powder and egg-white, and put on soft bandages; and put a ball of lead beside the hip if you are able to do so; then take a great band of palm width, and put on two layers of gauze over the bandages, and plaster; then take a thin splint of three fingers wide and long, and encircle that bundle, so that the head of the bundle is pendant; and put the splint on the trochanter, and turn the bundle over the collar, and take away the ball of lead from the hip, and from the painful hip; and leave the chest part alone, and when you see that the bandage holds the trochanter steadily, and that you clearly see that the splint does not move from the fractured bone, if the limb is properly immobilized, and when the limb is flexed, if the restraint is released; and manage the patient on his back, and put under his hip one small pillow beside the hip, to raise the limb up; if you align the fracture by aligning the shoulder blade, or you bind the arm to the collar, and do not release it until it is badly necessary.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Then resume the manipulation, if you see that it requires it, and hold and keep it still until it is restored; and it is usually restored in about twenty-six days, and in less time for most people.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When the scapula is broken or fractured, do not move it except by touch; if it appears according to the figure of the fracture, and is reset according to its natural form, in every way that you can; then put on the limb powder with abundant eggshell, and bandage lightly, and put on a double drape; then put on a broad and firm splint, wider than the scapula, and if the splint is not firmly secured in any part of the scapula, use the dressing of flaxseed, so that the splint rests evenly; and then strain it with a great firm bend, so that the splint does not move from its place, and look at the mark of each joint; and every time it relaxes, if you strain it, and put back the splint if it has gone out of place, and let the patient rest on his side; and the scapula is restored in XX days or in XXV, And when this number is completed, if the pain ceases, and so be cured, for it is not a bone that is easily broken.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	If a piece of the bone sticks out beforehand, and not a little, if it remains there, and the bone, do as we have said in the loosening of the forcele to appease the abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	If a piece of the bone sticks out beforehand, and not a little, if it remains there, and the bone, do as we have said in the loosening of the forcele to appease the abscess.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The body is never entirely broken in a thousand pieces, but this happens often; but it breaks often with a sudden movement.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	When it is broken in pieces, if it is downhill, and the patient experiences great pain, and weakness, vomiting blood, and opening the wound in the fractured bone, and feeling well again.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the patient lies supine on his back, place one cushion between the scapulae and press them together. Assemble the ribs with your hands, and with subtle force restore the bones to their normal position, ensuring that the bone is properly aligned. Then place on plaster bandages and stamp with fine salt, or other soft powder, and cover with a single bandage, and bind firmly over the fracture. Keep the patient still for an hour after reduction, and if it comes loose again, either through corrosion or inflammation, or pain or swelling, grasp and re-extend immediately, and if necessary remove the plaster. Wipe off the plaster, address the underlying cause of the fracture, and reapply the plaster.
de la brisure des costes	When the bones of the ribs are fractured.
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	The fractures of the ribs only come from a great fall from the back or from the head downwards, and they do not bruise except for this that they are slippery; and the patient feels well at the inquiry as two.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	The restoration is if you put the fracture back in its place, as it should be done
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put on a bandage and bind it with a splint if necessary
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is displaced downwards, if the patient feels great pain and tingling, like with pleurisy, because the bone is pressing on the gut; then there are vomiting and diarrhea with great loss of blood, which is a serious illness, and that often happens.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if you are told that it is necessary to administer nourishing foods that will swell the belly, to push out the fracture
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, except when the boil has burst, and only then.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has burst, if it is well.</start_of_turn>
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	They say that no one puts a bandage on the limb for its swelling, for it is like reason; however, there is doubt that the bandage will not draw out the superfluous matter from the limb by the force of weakness.</start_of_turn>
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	They say that no one should cover the limb with coarse cloth in oil, and put on tight bands between the ribs to measure equally the swelling between the ribs, then either cure with the poultice of pleurisin, of meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient experiences great pain that he cannot endure from the bone that points towards the navel, and there is doubt in the patient, if it is possible to cut above the fractured bone, and to put on a bandage to hold it in place; and then the bone must be cut, and treated lightly, and then the two layers of the wound must be sutured, if it is large, and it must be dressed with bandages until it has healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if pus comes from the wound, put on moist cloths soaked in rose oil, and put on a bandage; and cure while the limb coves with the wound, and do not leave the edge of the wound open, as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure dou col	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear from the bone that points to the navel, and there is doubt in the patient, if it is commanded to cut above the broken rib, and to put in [a foreign object] as a support; then one must cut the bone and remove it gently, and then suture the two layers of the wound, if it is large, and cure it with bandages, until it is healed. And if an abscess comes out, if put on moist cloths soaked in rose oil, and put on the wound; and cure while the bone that was cut is at rest, and do not move the ribs or it must, until it is healed. And if there is a fracture of the collarbone...
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Never comes a fracture of the collarbone as a sudden blow; and thus also with a thorn in the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to no avail, and you know if it will be healed or not, take care if you see his hands softened and limp and dead, and cannot move or extend, and when you prick them with a needle, if there is no sensation
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	The wound that is deadly in many situations, if you move it and feel well when you strain and prick it, the wound will be saved, and the patient will be cured, if you put on treatment.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if any other thing comes to the spine from behind, and you must know whether there is blood or not; if it is taken care of, if the wound is softened, and if the accident is on the hands or on the back, there should be an immediate suspension of the wind and vomiting with the will; and when it has been soothed on the belly, there should be an immediate vomiting with the will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it has been soothed on the back and it vomits, it must not be allowed to leave the bed.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	The patient must not work in his wound
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	If this accident does not happen, if the thing is less serious.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.
