Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	If it does not return by this treatment, take a cube of three fingers' length, and clamp the area below the navel, and let the patient lie on their side; place the head of the cube below the navel, then put the middle of the cube on the spine; and place the thumbs of both hands on the other head of the cube, and press firmly, until it returns to its place. If you see that it is not returning, do it at the point that is turning at the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	If two fingers grasp the head of the patient at the arm's end, and two others support the parts, and between each finger there are sowers and nails, one palm's length; and there is in each finger one hole, or the nail is twisted, and the fingers must be firmly fixed in place so that they do not move; and between two fingers there is one turning, so that the line that is between the shoulder blades and the turning point of the elbow must be returned to the turning point by two little fingers of one palm's length; and then join the line which is among the buttocks to the turning point towards the head, and the other line towards the parts towards the other turning point, and the minister grasps their turning point at all the line, and the master puts the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when they are even, if you put on a dry dressing with much yolk, and then press it, and then support it with a tablet of three fingers’ length, that will cause the swelling of the belly and the upper part of the spine to recede, and bind it with a thread as we have said; and use the patient with gentle nourishment until they are well; and if no other symptom appears at the end of the well-being, if it is necessary to administer soothing and calming medicines, with the support that we have said above; and in no case give a piece of lead, and in no case does the appearance come from behind the shoulder blade towards the loin, and take care that this is not a dislocation; for it is the bone that has opened, for which we must have no presumption: by chance comes death.
des dislocations de la hainche	hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	The hip joint and the shoulder joint only dislocate; this does not happen with other joints; and the hip joint is damaged in three parts: front and back, and top and bottom; the more damaged it is at the front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And if you know of a dislocation, when you join the painful limb with the belt, if it is longer and the patient’s knee is wider than the normal, and he cannot double his knee at the fire; and it is the cause of the elevation of the abscess to the buttock.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And thus knowing of his dislocation is this, that when one unites the afflicted limb with the flesh, if it is longer, and if the patient’s knee is greater than the fellow limb, and cannot bend his knee as before, this is a sign that this accident is contrary to the former ones.</start_of_turn>
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of the one who has it in front, if it is well his limb according to completion; nevertheless, do not double the knee joint because of pain, and if you see him do so, if you cannot prevent it beforehand, retain his urine, swell his ankle, and when he walks, let it pass over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of the one who has it behind, if he cannot extend his knee, do not double it, and that leg is shorter than the other, his ankle is soft, and his thigh bone is dislocated from its socket
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	We must return this semblance of dislocation if it is an old one, and it endures according to its setting, if there is no cure; and one must not presume otherwise.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in this case where the dislocation is fresh, and there are three ways of dislocation, if you are hasty you will tear the joint apart and stretch it inwards and outwards, and move it to the right and left; by chance if it returns, there is no need for any other cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, if you must know, that you must place two strong ministers, and put the limb firmly with two hands, or with one that is linked above the knee; and another minister extends his hand upwards as far as he can stretch his hands downwards towards his buttocks, and then grasp it with a loop of thread above the hip; and another holds the head of the limb; and extend upwards and downwards at the same time, until the patient is lifted from the earth at once, and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common in three out of four cases; and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.</start_of_turn>
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, if you can put the cure in its place; when the dislocation is in the armpit, you can hold the patient over his side, then put the limb on the root of the bone, and the bone which is above the knuckle, then stretch the limb upwards towards the armpit and towards the forcele; then grasp another assistant with his arms and embrace the great bone of the painful limb, and stretch it outwards: if it returns to its place now; this method is more gentle than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you do not manage to secure it in this manner as we have said, if you can tie the two feet of the patient together with a strong rope around the two toes and the two knees, and let the painful limb be extended twice as much as the others; then let it hang suspended from the head of a staff or from the ground with two long arms; then command one minister to embrace the head of the limb, and let another minister hang alongside the patient, who embraces the limb, for the joint will return naturally.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation. S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put on the table, and press on it as we have said in hydrops, and keep the patient on the cost of the table.

And when the dislocation is forward, if you must, extend the limb gently, as I have said; and look with your eye where I have said; and put your hand on the painful area of the limb, and press with the other hand, and extend from the knee towards the groin.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is displaced, if it does not succeed in extending the limb backwards, do not lift it from the ground, but know that it must be as it was before the displacement, as we have said concerning the two finger-nails; and be above the face, and the link must be extended as we have said before, and must press on the joint at the table; and it will be finished when the patient extends his limb, and they will be equal; then join the thighs and put on the dressing, and put on a bandage, so that the limb does not move; and leave it for three days or four, then remove it, and put on the dressing again; and if you see that they are equal, if the strain, as before, and leave it for three days; then remove it, and make the patient comfortable, as much as possible, until the limb is comfortable
de la dislocation dou genoil	As for the dislocation of the shoulder joint...
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture in two ways: frontally and laterally; and do not strain it forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez. de la dislocation dou talon	Until it is healed.
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The shoulder joint is never fully rigid and is never fully relaxed, but is always somewhat tense and painful.

And when it is completely dry, if you make the patient sit upright, and hold his foot firmly by the ankle; then bring the thumb to your right hand, then to the left hand twice, then extend it upwards, and keep it well stretched out; do this twice as we have said, at the end and while pulling the thumb; if it comes back, that is good; if not, repeat the work, for it will come back; and if it cannot come back, make the patient sit on his heels on the ground, and put his heel firmly on the ground between his thighs, and cover him with a blanket, so that he does not bleed; then hold the foot with one hand and another hand grasp the limb above the ankle, that it lies on the heel of the foot; then extend the toes equally, and tie them either tightly between the patient’s thighs to hold the patient when it is stretched; then put the eyes equally on the dislocation with your hands, and another assistant holds the limb steady at the ankle, and the dislocation will return immediately.

And if he goes before this end, it is not certain that it will not damage further.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If pus comes out of place, if you must know, you must calm it down, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	If pus comes out of place, if you must know, you must calm it down, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the joint is dislocated, if you must know, it is necessary to stretch the limb to resume its normal position, and this is a light matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in no other place than on the back of the limb, then you must make the patient sit on one leg or on a table perfectly straight, and put your limb on what is open of these joints, then press your limb firmly until it returns; and when it is even, and there is no opening, if you put on the foot of the limb on a table for two fingers, then the strain is formed, and leave it for three days, then take it off; and rest it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	And when they are even, and nothing is open, if you put charcoal from a pine tree onto a table at a quarter past twelve, then the strain will form, and leave it for two days, then take it out; and restore it until it is healed.
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with a dislocation, and it is seen to restore itself, many times it has happened that the patient died: if you are not wise in the cure and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and late, do not be ashamed; and at the beginning use soothing things about the wound, and leave the patient in the hands of God, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, if you remember now to restore the limb, so that the wound also heals; and when the limb is restored, if you administer soothing things about the wound, and cure the wound, as it should be, from dried pus; and if with the dislocation there is fracture, and bones are broken, if the bones are fractured, do as we have said in simple diseases; and beware of pride, as we have said, for this will bring you misery according to your Creator, and for the salvation of your soul and body.
Amen	Amen.
